Let's try to derive using complex numbers or coordinates but with a more clever choice: Use coordinate system with origin at M, and let the common chord be the y-axis. That is what we have: M = (0,0), N = (d,0), A = (x0, y0), B = (x0, -y0). We already have nice expressions: y_P = -p (x0+r)/y0, and H = (p, - (d-p) y0/(x0+r)). Also, v = (p-x0, y_P-y0). Compute v more explicitly.

We have v = (p - x0, y_P - y0) = (p - x0, -p (x0+r)/y0 - y0) = (p - x0, -(p (x0+r) + y0^2)/y0). And y0^2 = r^2 - x0^2.

So p (x0+r) + y0^2 = p(x0+r) + r^2 - x0^2 = p(x0+r) + (r-x0)(r+x0) = (x0+r)(p + r - x0). So v = (p - x0, -(x0+r)(p + r - x0)/y0).

Thus v = (p - x0, -(x0+r)(p + r - x0)/y0).

Now note that p + r - x0 =? p = (d+R-r)/2, so p+r = (d+R+r)/2. So p+r-x0 = (d+R+r)/2 - x0. Not sure.

But we can also compute the direction vector of AP: from A to P: (p-x0, y_P - y0). So that's v. So line ‚Ąď through H with direction v.

Now we need to show ‚Ąď is tangent to circle (BEF). So let's compute B, E, F.

B = (x0, -y0).

Now E = A + t_E v, where t_E = -2(A¬∑v)/|v|^2.

A¬∑v = (x0, y0) ¬∑ (p-x0, y_P - y0) = x0(p-x0) + y0(y_P - y0) = x0(p-x0) + y0 y_P - y0^2.

But y0 y_P = y0 * (-p (x0+r)/y0) = -p (x0+r). So A¬∑v = x0(p-x0) - p(x0+r) - y0^2 = x0 p - x0^2 - p x0 - p r - y0^2 = -x0^2 - p r - y0^2 = -(x0^2+y0^2) - p r = -r^2 - p r = -r(r+p). So A¬∑v = -r(p+r). Good simplification!

Thus t_E = -2(-r(p+r))/|v|^2 = 2r(p+r)/|v|^2.

Similarly, (A-N)¬∑v: A-N = (x0-d, y0). Then (A-N)¬∑v = (x0-d)(p-x0) + y0(y_P - y0) = (x0-d)(p-x0) + y0 y_P - y0^2. y0 y_P = -p(x0+r). So (A-N)¬∑v = (x0-d)(p-x0) - p(x0+r) - y0^2 = Expand: (x0-d)(p-x0) = (x0-d)p - (x0-d)x0 = p x0 - p d - x0^2 + d x0. Then subtract p(x0+r) gives: p x0 - p d - x0^2 + d x0 - p x0 - p r = -p d - x0^2 + d x0 - p r. Then subtract y0^2: = -p d - x0^2 + d x0 - p r - (r^2 - x0^2) = -p d - x0^2 + d x0 - p r - r^2 + x0^2 = -p d + d x0 - p r - r^2 = d(x0 - p) - r(p+r). But x0-p = -(p-x0). So d(x0-p) = -d(p-x0). So (A-N)¬∑v = -d(p-x0) - r(p+r). So (A-N)¬∑v = -[d(p-x0) + r(p+r)]. Then t_F = -2((A-N)¬∑v)/|v|^2 = -2(-[d(p-x0) + r(p+r)])/|v|^2 = 2(d(p-x0) + r(p+r))/|v|^2.

Thus we have:

E = A + (2r(p+r)/|v|^2) v
F = A + (2(d(p-x0) + r(p+r))/|v|^2) v

So both E and F are on line AP, as expected.

Now we need to find circle through B, E, F. That is a circle in the plane. Since B is the reflection of A across x-axis, and E, F lie on line AP, perhaps the circle (BEF) is symmetric in some way.

Let‚Äôs denote the line AP: param t with point X(t) = A + t v. Then A corresponds to t=0, P to t=1, E to t_E = 2r(p+r)/|v|^2, F to t_F = 2(d(p-x0) + r(p+r))/|v|^2.

Now B = (x0, -y0). Note that B is not on line AP generally.

Let u = őĪ-ő≥, v = ő≤-őī. Then line AB: u x + v y = 0. So direction vector: (v, -u). So B = t (v, -u) for some t ‚Č† 0. Then B lies on ő©: |B|^2 = 2őĪ B_x + 2ő≤ B_y. Compute:

|B|^2 = t^2 (v^2+u^2). B_x = t v, B_y = -t u.
RHS: 2őĪ t v + 2ő≤ (-t u) = 2t (őĪ v - ő≤ u). So equation: t^2 (u^2+v^2) = 2t (őĪ v - ő≤ u). Since t ‚Č† 0, we have t (u^2+v^2) = 2 (őĪ v - ő≤ u). So t = 2 (őĪ v - ő≤ u)/(u^2+v^2). Note that u^2+v^2 = |(őĪ-ő≥, ő≤-őī)|^2 = |N-M|^2 = |d|^2.

Thus B = (2 (őĪ v - ő≤ u) / |d|^2) * (v, -u). Alternatively, we can compute B directly.

Now, we have points:

B (some coordinates)
E = (2őĪ, 0)
F = (2ő≥, 0)

We need to find the circumcircle of triangle BEF. Since E and F lie on x-axis, the perpendicular bisector of EF is vertical line x = (2őĪ+2ő≥)/2 = őĪ+ő≥. So the circumcenter O = (őĪ+ő≥, o_y) for some o_y. And radius R = distance from O to E = sqrt((őĪ+ő≥-2őĪ)^2 + o_y^2) = sqrt((ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2). Also, O must satisfy distance to B equals R: |O - B|^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2.

Thus we can find o_y from equation:

(O_x - B_x)^2 + (O_y - B_y)^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2.

But O_x = őĪ+ő≥, O_y = o_y. So:

(őĪ+ő≥ - B_x)^2 + (o_y - B_y)^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2.

Expand: (őĪ+ő≥ - B_x)^2 + o_y^2 - 2 o_y B_y + B_y^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2.

Cancel o_y^2: (őĪ+ő≥ - B_x)^2 - 2 o_y B_y + B_y^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2.

Thus solve for o_y:

2 o_y B_y = (őĪ+ő≥ - B_x)^2 + B_y^2 - (ő≥-őĪ)^2.

So o_y = [ (őĪ+ő≥ - B_x)^2 + B_y^2 - (ő≥-őĪ)^2 ] / (2 B_y), provided B_y ‚Č† 0.

Now, we also need y_H, the y-coordinate of H (orthocenter of triangle PMN). Then the condition that the horizontal line y = y_H is tangent to circle (BEF) is that y_H = o_y ¬Ī R, i.e., (y_H - o_y)^2 = R^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2.

So we need to verify that (y_H - o_y)^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2.

This is equivalent to y_H^2 - 2 y_H o_y + o_y^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2 => y_H^2 - 2 y_H o_y = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 => 2 y_H o_y = y_H^2 - (ő≥-őĪ)^2 => o_y = (y_H^2 - (ő≥-őĪ)^2)/(2 y_H), provided y_H ‚Č† 0.

Thus if we can compute y_H and show that it satisfies that relation with o_y, we are done. So we need to find y_H in terms of őĪ,ő≤,ő≥,őī. And also compute o_y from B.

Given the time, I'll try to complete the analytic proof using the coordinate system with MN as x-axis, and compute O_BEF and then verify the tangency condition. This is heavy but we can use the simplifications we already have. Let's proceed.

Define |v|^2 = dx^2 + dy^2.

We also have H = (p, y_H) with y_H = - (d-p) y0/(x0+r).

Now, we need to find the circumcenter O of triangle BEF. Let‚Äôs denote:

E = (x_E, y_E) = (x0 + t_E dx, y0 + t_E dy)
F = (x_F, y_F) = (x0 + t_F dx, y0 + t_F dy)

Since E and F lie on line L: (x0, y0) + t v.

Now, B = (x0, -y0).

We can compute O. Since E and F are on L, the perpendicular bisector of EF is perpendicular to L at the midpoint of EF. Let‚Äôs denote t_mid = (t_E+t_F)/2. Then midpoint M_EF = (x0 + t_mid dx, y0 + t_mid dy). The direction vector of L is v = (dx, dy). A vector perpendicular to v is n = (dy, -dx). So O = M_EF + őľ n for some őľ.

We also have OB = OE (since O is circumcenter). So |O-B|^2 = |O-E|^2. This gives an equation to solve for őľ.

Let‚Äôs compute O - B and O - E.

Let‚Äôs define:

O = (x0 + t_mid dx + őľ dy, y0 + t_mid dy - őľ dx).

Then:

O - B = (x0 + t_mid dx + őľ dy - x0, y0 + t_mid dy - őľ dx + y0) = (t_mid dx + őľ dy, 2y0 + t_mid dy - őľ dx).

O - E = (x0 + t_mid dx + őľ dy - (x0 + t_E dx), y0 + t_mid dy - őľ dx - (y0 + t_E dy)) = ((t_mid - t_E) dx + őľ dy, (t_mid - t_E) dy - őľ dx).

Set |O-B|^2 = |O-E|^2.

Compute:

(t_mid dx + őľ dy)^2 + (2y0 + t_mid dy - őľ dx)^2 = ((t_mid - t_E) dx + őľ dy)^2 + ((t_mid - t_E) dy - őľ dx)^2.

Expand both sides. Let‚Äôs denote:

LHS = (t_mid dx)^2 + 2 t_mid dx őľ dy + őľ^2 dy^2 + (2y0)^2 + 2*2y0*(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + (t_mid dy - őľ dx)^2
= t_mid^2 dx^2 + 2 t_mid dx őľ dy + őľ^2 dy^2 + 4y0^2 + 4y0 t_mid dy - 4y0 őľ dx + (t_mid^2 dy^2 - 2 t_mid dy őľ dx + őľ^2 dx^2).

LHS = t_mid^2 (dx^2+dy^2) + őľ^2 (dx^2+dy^2) + 2 t_mid dx őľ dy - 2 t_mid dy őľ dx + 2 t_mid dy őľ dx? Wait, we have +2 t_mid dx őľ dy from first term, and -2 t_mid dy őľ dx from the last term? Actually the last term gives -2 t_mid dy őľ dx. So combine: 2 t_mid dx őľ dy - 2 t_mid dy őľ dx = 0? Because dx őľ dy = őľ dx dy, and dy őľ dx = őľ dx dy, so they cancel. So LHS = t_mid^2 |v|^2 + őľ^2 |v|^2 + 4y0^2 + 4y0 t_mid dy - 4y0 őľ dx.

Thus LHS = |v|^2 (t_mid^2 + őľ^2) + 4y0^2 + 4y0 t_mid dy - 4y0 őľ dx.

Now RHS: ((t_mid - t_E) dx + őľ dy)^2 + ((t_mid - t_E) dy - őľ dx)^2. Expand:

First term: (t_mid - t_E)^2 dx^2 + 2(t_mid - t_E) dx őľ dy + őľ^2 dy^2.
Second term: (t_mid - t_E)^2 dy^2 - 2(t_mid - t_E) dy őľ dx + őľ^2 dx^2.

Sum: (t_mid - t_E)^2 (dx^2+dy^2) + őľ^2 (dx^2+dy^2) + 2(t_mid - t_E) őľ (dx dy - dy dx) = (t_mid - t_E)^2 |v|^2 + őľ^2 |v|^2 + 0. So RHS = |v|^2 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2).

Set LHS = RHS:

|v|^2 (t_mid^2 + őľ^2) + 4y0^2 + 4y0 t_mid dy - 4y0 őľ dx = |v|^2 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2).

Cancel őľ^2 |v|^2 both sides:

|v|^2 t_mid^2 + 4y0^2 + 4y0 t_mid dy - 4y0 őľ dx = |v|^2 (t_mid - t_E)^2.

Thus:

|v|^2 (t_mid^2 - (t_mid - t_E)^2) = -4y0^2 - 4y0 t_mid dy + 4y0 őľ dx.

But t_mid^2 - (t_mid - t_E)^2 = t_mid^2 - (t_mid^2 - 2 t_mid t_E + t_E^2) = 2 t_mid t_E - t_E^2 = t_E (2 t_mid - t_E).

So:

|v|^2 t_E (2 t_mid - t_E) = -4y0^2 - 4y0 t_mid dy + 4y0 őľ dx.

Thus we can solve for őľ:

4y0 őľ dx = |v|^2 t_E (2 t_mid - t_E) + 4y0^2 + 4y0 t_mid dy.

So őľ = [ |v|^2 t_E (2 t_mid - t_E) + 4y0^2 + 4y0 t_mid dy ] / (4y0 dx).

Now, we also have t_mid = (t_E+t_F)/2. And we have expressions for t_E, t_F in terms of |v|^2. This may simplify.

Let's compute t_E and t_F in terms of |v|^2 and the other parameters.

We have:

t_E = 2r(p+r)/|v|^2.
t_F = 2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/|v|^2.

Thus t_E and t_F are known.

Also, p = (d+R-r)/2, x0 = (d^2 - R^2 + r^2)/(2d). We also have y0^2 = r^2 - x0^2.

We might need to compute |v|^2 = dx^2+dy^2. We have dx = p - x0, dy = y_P - y0 = -p(x0+r)/y0 - y0 = -(p(x0+r)+y0^2)/y0. And we have y0^2 = r^2 - x0^2. So p(x0+r)+y0^2 = p(x0+r)+r^2-x0^2 = p(x0+r)+(r-x0)(r+x0) = (x0+r)(p+r-x0). So dy = -(x0+r)(p+r-x0)/y0.

Thus őľ = [ |v|^2 t_E t_F + 4y0^2 + 4y0 t_mid dy ] / (4y0 dx). Good.

- The circle (ACD) (passes through A) maps to line ‚Ąď3 through C' and D'.
- The point P (circumcenter of ACD) is the center of the circle (ACD). Under inversion, the center of a circle through A does not map to the center of the line; but there is a known: The inverse of the center of a circle through the inversion center is the orthocenter of the triangle formed by the images of the other two points? Actually, consider circle with center O passing through A. Invert about A. The circle becomes a line ‚Ąď. The point O inverts to some point O'. The triangle formed by A, C, D? Not.

Let's use complex numbers: Inversion about A with radius 1 (for convenience). Then for any point X, X' = (X-A)/(\overline{X-A})? Actually, inversion is not analytic; but if we compose with reflection, we can use complex numbers: Inversion about A with radius 1 sends z to A + 1/(\overline{z-A})? That's a composition of inversion and reflection. To avoid that, we can use the transformation: z' = (z - A) / (|z-A|^2)? That's not analytic.

Given the complexity, I think the coordinate proof is the way to go, but we need to present it clearly, with careful algebraic simplifications. Since the problem is from an olympiad, a coordinate solution is acceptable if done rigorously. Let's attempt to produce a clean coordinate proof.

We set up coordinates:

Let M = (0,0), N = (d,0) with d > 0. Let ő©: x^2 + y^2 = r^2, őď: (x-d)^2 + y^2 = R^2, with r < R and |R-r| < d < R+r. The circles intersect at A and B. By symmetry, we can choose A = (x0, y0) with y0 > 0, B = (x0, -y0), where x0 = (d^2 - R^2 + r^2)/(2d), y0 = sqrt(r^2 - x0^2) > 0.

Now, the line MN is the x-axis. It meets ő© at C = (-r,0) and őď at D = (d+R,0), with order C, M, N, D. So C = (-r,0), D = (d+R,0).

Now, define P as circumcenter of triangle ACD. Since C and D lie on x-axis, the perpendicular bisector of CD is vertical line x = (C_x + D_x)/2 = ( -r + d+R )/2 = (d+R-r)/2 = p. So P has x-coordinate p. Let P = (p, y_P). Since PA = PC, we have (x0-p)^2 + (y0-y_P)^2 = (-r-p)^2 + y_P^2. Expanding gives -2x0p + x0^2 + y0^2 -2y0y_P + y_P^2 = p^2 + 2pr + r^2 + y_P^2. Cancel y_P^2 and use x0^2+y0^2 = r^2. Then we get -2x0p + r^2 -2y0y_P = p^2 + 2pr + r^2 => -2x0p -2y0y_P = p^2 + 2pr => 2y0y_P = -p^2 -2pr -2x0p = -p(p+2r+2x0). So y_P = -p(p+2r+2x0)/(2y0). But we earlier found y_P = -p(x0+r)/y0. Let's check consistency: p(p+2r+2x0)/(2y0) = p(p+2r+2x0)/(2y0). Is that equal to p(x0+r)/y0? That would require p+2r+2x0 = 2(x0+r) => p+2r+2x0 = 2x0+2r => p=0, which is not. So there is a discrepancy. Let's re-derive carefully.

We have C = (-r, 0), D = (d+R, 0). Their midpoint: x = (-r + d+R)/2 = p. So perpendicular bisector of CD: x = p. So P = (p, y_P). Now, condition PA = PC: distance from P to A equals distance from P to C.

PA^2 = (x0-p)^2 + (y0-y_P)^2.
PC^2 = (-r-p)^2 + (0-y_P)^2 = (p+r)^2 + y_P^2. (since -r-p = -(p+r), square = (p+r)^2).

Set equal:

(x0-p)^2 + y0^2 - 2y0 y_P + y_P^2 = (p+r)^2 + y_P^2.

Cancel y_P^2:

(x0-p)^2 + y0^2 - 2y0 y_P = (p+r)^2.

Now, (x0-p)^2 = x0^2 - 2x0p + p^2. So:

x0^2 - 2x0p + p^2 + y0^2 - 2y0 y_P = p^2 + 2pr + r^2.

Cancel p^2:

x0^2 + y0^2 - 2x0p - 2y0 y_P = 2pr + r^2.

But x0^2+y0^2 = r^2. So:

r^2 - 2x0p - 2y0 y_P = 2pr + r^2 => -2x0p - 2y0 y_P = 2pr => Divide 2: -x0p - y0 y_P = pr => Thus y0 y_P = -pr - x0p = -p(r+x0). So y_P = -p(r+x0)/y0.

That matches our earlier expression. Good. So we have y_P = -p (r+x0)/y0.

Now, note that r+x0 > 0 because x0 ‚Č• -r, and if x0 = -r then A is at (-r,y0) with y0=0? Actually if x0=-r, then y0^2 = r^2 - r^2 =0, so A = (-r,0)=C, which would be degenerate. So x0 > -r, so r+x0 >0. So y_P <0.

Now, line AP: through A(x0,y0) and P(p, y_P). Its direction vector v = (p-x0, y_P-y0). We'll keep it.

Now, let's find E and F as second intersections of line AP with ő© and őď.

Parameterize line AP: X(t) = A + t v, t real. For t=0: A; t=1: P. For ő©: |X(t)|^2 = r^2. Since |A|^2 = r^2, we have |A + t v|^2 = r^2 + 2t (A¬∑v) + t^2 |v|^2 = r^2 => 2t (A¬∑v) + t^2 |v|^2 = 0 => t(2A¬∑v + t|v|^2)=0. Non-zero root: t_E = -2(A¬∑v)/|v|^2. Compute A¬∑v = x0(p-x0) + y0(y_P-y0). But y0 y_P = -p(r+x0). So y0 y_P - y0^2 = -p(r+x0) - y0^2. So A¬∑v = x0(p-x0) - p(r+x0) - y0^2 = x0p - x0^2 - pr - px0 - y0^2 = -x0^2 - pr - y0^2 = -(x0^2+y0^2) - pr = -r^2 - pr = -r(p+r). So A¬∑v = -r(p+r). Thus t_E = -2(-r(p+r))/|v|^2 = 2r(p+r)/|v|^2.

Similarly, for őď: (X(t)-N)^2 = R^2. N=(d,0). So (A+N? Actually, (A - N + t v)^2 = R^2. Since |A-N|^2 = R^2, we get 2t ( (A-N)¬∑v ) + t^2 |v|^2 = 0 => t_F = -2((A-N)¬∑v)/|v|^2. Compute (A-N)¬∑v = (x0-d)(p-x0) + y0(y_P-y0). Using the same expansion as before: (x0-d)(p-x0) = (x0-d)p - (x0-d)x0 = p x0 - p d - x0^2 + d x0. Then add y0(y_P-y0) = y0 y_P - y0^2 = -p(r+x0) - y0^2. So sum = p x0 - p d - x0^2 + d x0 - p r - p x0 - y0^2 = - p d - x0^2 + d x0 - p r - y0^2 = - p d + d x0 - p r - (x0^2+y0^2) = -p d + d x0 - p r - r^2 = d(x0-p) - r(p+r). But x0-p = -(p-x0). So (A-N)¬∑v = -d(p-x0) - r(p+r). Thus t_F = -2(-d(p-x0)-r(p+r))/|v|^2 = 2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/|v|^2.

So t_E and t_F as given.

Now, define H, orthocenter of triangle PMN. M=(0,0), N=(d,0), P=(p, y_P). Since M and N are on x-axis, the altitude from P is vertical line x=p. So H lies on x=p. Let H = (p, y_H). The altitude from M is perpendicular to PN. PN vector: N-P = (d-p, -y_P). So altitude from M: through M, direction perpendicular to PN, i.e., vector (y_P, d-p) (since dot with PN: (d-p)*y_P + (-y_P)*(d-p)=0). So line: (x,y)= (0,0)+s(y_P, d-p). This line meets x=p at s = p/y_P? Actually, x = s y_P = p => s = p/y_P. Then y = s(d-p) = p(d-p)/y_P. So y_H = p(d-p)/y_P. Since y_P < 0, y_H < 0. So H = (p, p(d-p)/y_P).

We can also compute y_H using that y_P = -p(r+x0)/y0. So y_H = p(d-p) / ( -p(r+x0)/y0 ) = - (d-p) y0/(r+x0). That matches earlier expression: y_H = - (d-p) y0/(x0+r). Good.

Now, we need to prove that line ‚Ąď through H parallel to AP (direction v) is tangent to circumcircle of triangle BEF.

Let‚Äôs compute the circle (BEF). We'll find its circumcenter O and radius R. Because the line ‚Ąď is parallel to v, we can consider the condition that the distance from O to ‚Ąď equals R. But maybe we can find a relationship: The point A is the midpoint of the arc EF of the circle (BEF)? Not.

Let's try to compute O using the perpendicular bisector method we started earlier. We have:

Now, we also have OB = OE. Using our earlier derivation, we found őľ = - [ |v|^2 (t_mid - t_E)^2 - |(0,2y0) + t_mid v|^2 ] / (4 y0 dx). But we can simplify using t_mid - t_E = (t_F - t_E)/2.

We also have that |(0,2y0) + t_mid v|^2 = 4y0^2 + t_mid^2 |v|^2 + 4y0 t_mid dy.

Now, we can compute |v|^2 (t_mid - t_E)^2 = |v|^2 ((t_F - t_E)^2/4) = (|v|^2/4)(t_F - t_E)^2.

Thus the numerator becomes (|v|^2/4)(t_F - t_E)^2 - [4y0^2 + t_mid^2 |v|^2 + 4y0 t_mid dy].

Now, note that t_F - t_E = 2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L - 2r(p+r)/L = 2(d(p-x0))/L. So t_F - t_E = 2d(p-x0)/L. And L = |v|^2.

Thus t_F - t_E = 2d(p-x0)/L.

Then (t_F - t_E)^2 = 4d^2(p-x0)^2/L^2.

So (|v|^2/4)(t_F - t_E)^2 = (L/4)* (4d^2(p-x0)^2/L^2) = d^2(p-x0)^2/L.

Thus t_mid = (d(p-x0)+2r(p+r))/L.

We can compute B coordinates in terms of őĪ,ő≤,ő≥,őī. Then we need to compute H, orthocenter of triangle PMN, with P=(p,0) on x-axis. Now, we have the relation that P is circumcenter of triangle ACD. In this coordinate system, A=0, P=(p,0). And we have C and D are points on line MN (centers) and on circles. We can compute C and D in terms of M,N. The condition that P is circumcenter gives:

p C_x = |C|^2/2, p D_x = |D|^2/2.

Thus we have two equations that determine p and also give a relation between M,N. So we can solve for p.

Now, we can also compute H: orthocenter of triangle PMN. Since M=(őĪ,ő≤), N=(ő≥,őī), P=(p,0). The orthocenter H can be computed using the formula: H = M + N + P - 2 O, where O is circumcenter of triangle PMN. But we can also compute H directly as intersection of altitudes. Since P is on x-axis, altitude from P is perpendicular to MN. So H lies on line through P perpendicular to MN. That line is given by: (x,y) = (p,0) + u (őī-ő≤, -(ő≥-őĪ))? Actually, direction vector perpendicular to MN = (ő≥-őĪ, őī-ő≤) is (őī-ő≤, -(ő≥-őĪ)). So line: (p + u(őī-ő≤), -u(ő≥-őĪ)). So H = (p + u_H (őī-ő≤), -u_H (ő≥-őĪ)). Now, also H must lie on altitude from M, which is perpendicular to PN. PN vector: N-P = (ő≥-p, őī). So altitude from M: through M, direction perpendicular to PN: (őī, -(ő≥-p)). So line: (őĪ,ő≤) + s (őī, -(ő≥-p)). The intersection gives equations.

Alternatively, we can compute y_H = -u_H (ő≥-őĪ). So we need u_H.

Now, we also have B = (x_B, y_B) from earlier: B = t (v, -u) with u = őĪ-ő≥, v = ő≤-őī, t = 2(őĪ v - ő≤ u)/L^2, where L^2 = u^2+v^2.

Now, the circle (BEF): E=(2őĪ,0), F=(2ő≥,0), B=(x_B,y_B). Its circumcenter O = (őĪ+ő≥, o_y) because perpendicular bisector of EF is vertical x = őĪ+ő≥. So O_x = őĪ+ő≥. And radius R = distance from O to E = sqrt((őĪ+ő≥-2őĪ)^2 + o_y^2) = sqrt((ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2). Also, OB = R gives:

(őĪ+ő≥ - x_B)^2 + (o_y - y_B)^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2.

Simplify:

(őĪ+ő≥ - x_B)^2 + o_y^2 - 2 o_y y_B + y_B^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2

=> (őĪ+ő≥ - x_B)^2 - 2 o_y y_B + y_B^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2

=> 2 o_y y_B = (őĪ+ő≥ - x_B)^2 + y_B^2 - (ő≥-őĪ)^2

=> o_y = [ (őĪ+ő≥ - x_B)^2 + y_B^2 - (ő≥-őĪ)^2 ] / (2 y_B), assuming y_B ‚Č† 0.

Now, the horizontal line through H is y = y_H. For it to be tangent to circle (BEF), we need |y_H - o_y| = R = sqrt((ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2). This is equivalent to (y_H - o_y)^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2 => y_H^2 - 2 y_H o_y + o_y^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2 => y_H^2 - 2 y_H o_y = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 => 2 y_H o_y = y_H^2 - (ő≥-őĪ)^2 => o_y = (y_H^2 - (ő≥-őĪ)^2)/(2 y_H). So we need to verify that the expression for o_y from B satisfies this.

Thus we need to compute y_H and then check that the o_y computed from B satisfies that relation. So we need to compute p and y_H in terms of őĪ,ő≤,ő≥,őī. Then compute B in terms of őĪ,ő≤,ő≥,őī. Then compute o_y and then show that o_y = (y_H^2 - (ő≥-őĪ)^2)/(2 y_H). That is an algebraic identity.

Let's attempt to derive p from the condition that P is circumcenter of ACD.

In the A=0, AP=x-axis system, we have A=0, P=(p,0). The points C and D are on line MN (through M and N). Let's compute M and N coordinates. We have:

M = (őĪ,ő≤)
N = (ő≥,őī)

Define d = N-M = (ő≥-őĪ, őī-ő≤). L = |d|.

Now, C = M - (r/L) d, where r = |M| = sqrt(őĪ^2+ő≤^2).
D = M + (1+R/L) d, where R = |N| = sqrt(ő≥^2+őī^2).

Now, condition P is circumcenter of ACD. Since A=0, we have:

P¬∑C = |C|^2/2  => p C_x = |C|^2/2
P¬∑D = |D|^2/2  => p D_x = |D|^2/2

Thus we have:

C_x = |C|^2/(2p)
D_x = |D|^2/(2p)

Now, compute C_x and |C|^2. As before:

|C|^2 = 2r^2 - (2r/L) M¬∑d, and M¬∑d = (R^2 - r^2 - L^2)/2.
So |C|^2 = 2r^2 - (2r/L)*((R^2 - r^2 - L^2)/2) = 2r^2 - (r/L)(R^2 - r^2 - L^2) = 2r^2 - (rR^2)/L + (r^3)/L + rL.

Also, C_x = őĪ - (r/L)(ő≥-őĪ) = őĪ - (r/L)(ő≥-őĪ).

Thus p = |C|^2/(2C_x). So p = [2r^2 - (rR^2)/L + (r^3)/L + rL] / [2(őĪ - (r/L)(ő≥-őĪ))].

This is still messy. But perhaps we can find a simpler expression for p by using the fact that P is also the circumcenter of triangle ACD, so it is the center of the circle through A, C, D. In complex numbers, if A=0, then the circumcenter is given by (c d (cŐĄ - dŐĄ))/(c dŐĄ - cŐĄ d). So p = (c d (cŐĄ - dŐĄ))/(c dŐĄ - cŐĄ d). Since p is real (on x-axis), this gives a condition.

But maybe we can avoid explicit p by using the fact that the line through H parallel to AP is tangent to (BEF). This might be equivalent to some cross ratio being harmonic, or that the point H is the midpoint of the segment connecting the centers of the circles? Not.

Now, E = A + t_E v, F = A + t_F v.

We want to find the circumcenter O of triangle BEF. Since B = (x0, -y0), E = (x0 + t_E dx, y0 + t_E dy), F = (x0 + t_F dx, y0 + t_F dy). Let‚Äôs denote:

Let‚Äôs denote:

Let a = t_E, b = t_F. Then E = (a dx, a dy), F = (b dx, b dy). And B = (0, -2y0).

Now, the circumcenter O' of triangle BEF. Since E and F lie on line through origin with direction v, the perpendicular bisector of EF is the line through the midpoint of EF, perpendicular to v. That midpoint is M_EF = ((a+b)/2 dx, (a+b)/2 dy) = t_mid v, where t_mid = (a+b)/2. The direction perpendicular to v is n = (dy, -dx). So O' = t_mid v + őľ n for some őľ.

Now, O' must satisfy that distance to B equals distance to E (or F). So |O' - B|^2 = |O' - E|^2.

Compute O' - B = t_mid v + őľ n - (0, -2y0) = t_mid v + őľ n + (0, 2y0) (since minus B gives + (0, 2y0)? Actually, B = (0, -2y0), so O' - B = (t_mid dx + őľ dy, t_mid dy - őľ dx) - (0, -2y0) = (t_mid dx + őľ dy, t_mid dy - őľ dx + 2y0). And O' - E = (t_mid v + őľ n) - (a v) = (t_mid - a) v + őľ n.

Now, as before, v¬∑n=0. So |O'-E|^2 = (t_mid - a)^2 |v|^2 + őľ^2 |v|^2 = |v|^2 ((t_mid - a)^2 + őľ^2).

And |O'-B|^2 = |(t_mid dx + őľ dy, t_mid dy - őľ dx + 2y0)|^2 = (t_mid dx + őľ dy)^2 + (t_mid dy - őľ dx + 2y0)^2.

Expand:

= t_mid^2 dx^2 + 2 t_mid dx őľ dy + őľ^2 dy^2 + (t_mid dy - őľ dx)^2 + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2

= t_mid^2 dx^2 + 2 t_mid dx őľ dy + őľ^2 dy^2 + t_mid^2 dy^2 - 2 t_mid dy őľ dx + őľ^2 dx^2 + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2

= |v|^2 (t_mid^2 + őľ^2) + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2.

Set equal to |v|^2 ((t_mid - a)^2 + őľ^2). Cancel őľ^2 |v|^2:

|v|^2 t_mid^2 + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2 = |v|^2 (t_mid - a)^2.

Thus:

4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) = |v|^2 ((t_mid - a)^2 - t_mid^2) - 4y0^2.

Compute ((t_mid - a)^2 - t_mid^2) = (t_mid^2 - 2t_mid a + a^2) - t_mid^2 = -2t_mid a + a^2 = a(a - 2t_mid). But note that a = t_E, and t_mid = (a+b)/2, so a - 2t_mid = a - (a+b) = -b. So ((t_mid - a)^2 - t_mid^2) = a(-b) = -a b.

Thus:

4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) = |v|^2 (-a b) - 4y0^2 = -ab |v|^2 - 4y0^2.

So:

4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) = -ab |v|^2 - 4y0^2.

Thus:

t_mid dy - őľ dx = - (ab |v|^2 + 4y0^2)/(4y0).

Now, we can solve for őľ:

őľ dx = t_mid dy + (ab |v|^2 + 4y0^2)/(4y0).

Thus őľ = [ t_mid dy + (ab |v|^2 + 4y0^2)/(4y0) ] / dx, provided dx ‚Č† 0. In our numeric, dx>0.

Let's attempt to compute the condition using the fact that the line ‚Ąď is tangent to circle (BEF) iff the equation for the intersection of ‚Ąď and the circle has discriminant zero. That is:

| (H - O) + s v |^2 = R^2.

We can compute the discriminant in terms of the dot products. The discriminant őĒ = 4[ (H-O)¬∑v ]^2 - 4|v|^2 (|H-O|^2 - R^2) = 0 => [ (H-O)¬∑v ]^2 = |v|^2 (|H-O|^2 - R^2).

Now, we can compute H-O and R. We have O = circumcenter of BEF. In the translated system with A=0, we have O' = t_mid v + őľ n. And H' = H - A = (dx, y_H - y0). And we have B' = (0, -2y0). Also, we have expressions for t_mid, őľ, etc. So we need to compute O' - H' and then the dot product with v.

Given that we have explicit formulas for t_mid and őľ, we can compute (H'-O')¬∑v = - (O'-H')¬∑v. So we need (O'-H')¬∑v. But O' = t_mid v + őľ n, so (O'-H')¬∑v = t_mid |v|^2 + őľ (n¬∑v) - H'¬∑v. Since n¬∑v=0, we get = t_mid |v|^2 - H'¬∑v. Thus (H'-O')¬∑v = -t_mid |v|^2 + H'¬∑v.

Now, compute H'¬∑v = (dx, y_H - y0)¬∑(dx, dy) = dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy = dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy.

Thus (H'-O')¬∑v = -t_mid |v|^2 + dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy.

Now, we also need |H'-O'|^2 - R^2. R^2 = |O'-B'|^2 = |(t_mid v + őľ n) - (0, -2y0)|^2 = |t_mid v + őľ n + (0, 2y0)|^2. As before, |O'-B'|^2 = |v|^2 (t_mid^2+őľ^2) + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2. But we also have that O' is the circumcenter, so OB' = OE' = etc. But we can compute |H'-O'|^2 - R^2 = |(H'-O')|^2 - |O'-B'|^2.

We can compute (H'-O') = H' - (t_mid v + őľ n) = (H' - t_mid v) - őľ n.

Then |H'-O'|^2 = |H' - t_mid v|^2 + őľ^2 |n|^2 - 2őľ (H' - t_mid v)¬∑ n.

Since n¬∑v=0, we have H'¬∑n =? H' = (dx, y_H - y0). n = (dy, -dx). So H'¬∑n = dx dy + (y_H - y0)(-dx) = dx dy - dx(y_H - y0) = dx (dy - y_H + y0). Also, t_mid v¬∑n =0. So (H' - t_mid v)¬∑ n = H'¬∑n.

Thus |H'-O'|^2 = |H' - t_mid v|^2 + őľ^2 |v|^2 - 2őľ H'¬∑n.

Now, |H' - t_mid v|^2 = |H'|^2 + t_mid^2 |v|^2 - 2 t_mid H'¬∑v.

So |H'-O'|^2 = |H'|^2 + t_mid^2 |v|^2 - 2 t_mid H'¬∑v + őľ^2 |v|^2 - 2őľ H'¬∑n.

Then |H'-O'|^2 - R^2 = [|H'|^2 + t_mid^2 |v|^2 - 2 t_mid H'¬∑v + őľ^2 |v|^2 - 2őľ H'¬∑n] - [|v|^2 (t_mid^2+őľ^2) + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2] = |H'|^2 - 2 t_mid H'¬∑v - 2őľ H'¬∑n - 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) - 4y0^2.

Simplify: |H'|^2 = dx^2 + (y_H - y0)^2.

And H'¬∑v = dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy.

Thus -2 t_mid H'¬∑v = -2 t_mid (dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy). So the expression becomes:

|H'|^2 - 2 t_mid H'¬∑v - 2őľ H'¬∑n - 4y0 t_mid dy + 4y0 őľ dx - 4y0^2.

= |H'|^2 - 2 t_mid (dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy) - 2őľ H'¬∑n - 4y0 t_mid dy + 4y0 őľ dx - 4y0^2.

Now, |H'|^2 = dx^2 + (y_H - y0)^2. So combine with -2 t_mid dx^2: = dx^2 (1-2t_mid) + (y_H - y0)^2 - 2 t_mid (y_H - y0) dy - 2őľ H'¬∑n - 4y0 t_mid dy + 4y0 őľ dx - 4y0^2.

Thus |H'-O'|^2 - R^2 = dx^2 (1-2t_mid) + (y_H - y0)^2 - 2 t_mid (y_H - y0) dy - 2őľ H'¬∑n - 4y0 t_mid dy + 4y0 őľ dx - 4y0^2.

Now, we also need the left side of the tangency condition: [ (H'-O')¬∑v ]^2 = |v|^2 (|H'-O'|^2 - R^2). But we already have (H'-O')¬∑v = -t_mid |v|^2 + H'¬∑v = -t_mid L + (dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy), where L = |v|^2.

So (H'-O')¬∑v = -t_mid L + dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy.

Thus we need to verify:

(-t_mid L + dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy)^2 = L ( |H'-O'|^2 - R^2 ).

That is a messy equation. However, we have explicit expressions for t_mid and őľ in terms of a,b, etc. And we have a,b = t_E, t_F. So we can plug in.

Let me try to understand the configuration deeper.

We have two circles ő© and őď intersecting at A and B. Let the line through the centers MN intersect the circles at C (on ő©) and D (on őď), with order C-M-N-D. So C is on the ray from M away from N, D is on the ray from N away from M. Then P is circumcenter of triangle ACD. So P is the center of the circle through A, C, D. Since C and D are on the line of centers, the circle (ACD) has its center on the perpendicular bisector of CD, which is a line perpendicular to MN. So P lies on a line perpendicular to MN. In fact, the perpendicular bisector of CD is the line through the midpoint of CD perpendicular to CD. Since CD is on MN, the perpendicular bisector is perpendicular to MN. So P lies on that line.

Now, consider the homothety with center A that sends ő© to őď. Under this homothety, the point C (on ő©) maps to some point C' on őď. Since C is on MN, and the homothety sends line MN to a line parallel to MN, the image C' lies on a line through A parallel to MN. But D is also on őď and on MN. So D and C' are both on őď, but generally not the same. So the homothety does not map C to D.

Now, consider the circle (ACD) centered at P. Its radius is PA. The line AP is a chord of this circle. The points E and F are the second intersections of AP with ő© and őď. So we have AE and AF are chords of ő© and őď. Since PA = PC = PD, we have that P is equidistant from A, C, D. So the circle (ACD) is the circumcircle of triangle ACD, with center P.

Now, note that the triangle PMN: M and N are centers of ő© and őď. Since P is on the perpendicular bisector of CD, which is perpendicular to MN, the line through P perpendicular to MN is the line that is the perpendicular bisector of CD. So PH is vertical. H is orthocenter of triangle PMN, so H lies on the altitude from P. So H is the foot of the altitude? No, orthocenter is intersection of altitudes. Since M,N are on x-axis, the altitude from P is vertical line x=p, so H has x=p. So H is on that vertical line.

Now, the line through H parallel to AP is ‚Ąď. So ‚Ąď is a line through H with the same slope as AP.

We need to show that ‚Ąď is tangent to circle (BEF). Perhaps we can show that ‚Ąď is the line through H that is symmetric to the line through A and the circumcenter of triangle PMN? Not.

Since M and N are on x-axis, the reflection of H over MN is the point that is the midpoint of the arc? Not.

I'll define:

Let M = (0,0), N = (d,0) with d > 0. Let r = |M A|? Actually, we have ő©: x^2+y^2 = r^2, őď: (x-d)^2+y^2 = R^2, with r < R and |R-r| < d < R+r. Let A = (x0, y0) with y0 > 0, B = (x0, -y0). Then x0 = (d^2 - R^2 + r^2)/(2d), y0 = sqrt(r^2 - x0^2) > 0.

Define p = (d+R-r)/2, so that C = (-r,0), D = (d+R,0) and the perpendicular bisector of CD is x = p.

Now, P is the circumcenter of triangle ACD. Since C and D lie on x-axis, the perpendicular bisector of CD is x = p, so P has x-coordinate p. Let P = (p, y_P). From PA = PC, we have (x0-p)^2 + (y0-y_P)^2 = (p+r)^2 + y_P^2. Expanding gives (x0-p)^2 + y0^2 - 2y0y_P + y_P^2 = p^2+2pr+r^2+y_P^2. Using x0^2+y0^2 = r^2, we get -2x0p + r^2 -2y0y_P = 2pr + r^2 => -2x0p -2y0y_P = 2pr => y0y_P = -p(x0+r) => y_P = -p(x0+r)/y0.

Thus P = (p, -p(x0+r)/y0).

Now, line AP: direction v = (p-x0, y_P - y0). We'll denote v = (dx, dy). Then t_E = 2r(p+r)/|v|^2, t_F = 2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/|v|^2. So E = A + t_E v, F = A + t_F v.

Now, H is orthocenter of triangle PMN. M=(0,0), N=(d,0), P=(p, y_P). The altitude from P is vertical line x=p. The altitude from M is perpendicular to PN. PN vector = (d-p, -y_P). A direction vector perpendicular to PN is (y_P, d-p). So altitude from M: parametric (0,0)+s(y_P, d-p). Setting x = p gives s = p/y_P. Then y = s(d-p) = p(d-p)/y_P. Thus H = (p, p(d-p)/y_P). Since y_P < 0, we have H_y = p(d-p)/y_P < 0. So H = (p, h_y) with h_y = p(d-p)/y_P.

Now, we need to prove that the line ‚Ąď through H parallel to v is tangent to the circumcircle of triangle BEF.

We will compute the circumcircle of BEF. Let‚Äôs denote:

B = (x0, -y0)
E = (x0 + t_E dx, y0 + t_E dy)
F = (x0 + t_F dx, y0 + t_F dy)

We'll find the circumcenter O of triangle BEF. Since E and F lie on the line L through A with direction v, and B is the reflection of A across the x-axis, we can use the following approach: Consider the translation that sends A to the origin. Define new coordinates:

Let X' = X - A. Then:

A' = (0,0)
B' = (0, -2y0)
E' = (t_E dx, t_E dy)
F' = (t_F dx, t_F dy)

Now, we need to find the circumcenter O' of triangle B'E'F'. Since B' is on the y-axis, and E',F' are on the line through origin with direction v, the perpendicular bisector of E'F' is the line through the midpoint of E'F' perpendicular to v. Let‚Äôs denote:

t_mid = (t_E + t_F)/2.
M_EF = t_mid v = (t_mid dx, t_mid dy).
Let n = (dy, -dx), which is perpendicular to v. Then O' = t_mid v + őľ n for some őľ.

Now, O' must satisfy that |O' - B'|^2 = |O' - E'|^2. We can solve for őľ.

Compute:

|O' - E'|^2 = | (t_mid - t_E) v + őľ n |^2 = (t_mid - t_E)^2 |v|^2 + őľ^2 |v|^2 (since v¬∑n=0). So = |v|^2 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2).

Now, |O' - B'|^2 = | t_mid v + őľ n - (0, -2y0) |^2 = | t_mid v + őľ n + (0, 2y0) |^2 = (t_mid dx + őľ dy)^2 + (t_mid dy - őľ dx + 2y0)^2.

Expand:

= t_mid^2 dx^2 + 2 t_mid dx őľ dy + őľ^2 dy^2 + (t_mid dy - őľ dx)^2 + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2

= t_mid^2 (dx^2+dy^2) + őľ^2 (dx^2+dy^2) + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2

= |v|^2 (t_mid^2 + őľ^2) + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2.

Set equal to |v|^2 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2). Cancel őľ^2 |v|^2:

|v|^2 t_mid^2 + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2 = |v|^2 (t_mid - t_E)^2.

Thus:

4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) = |v|^2 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 - t_mid^2) - 4y0^2.

Compute ((t_mid - t_E)^2 - t_mid^2) = (t_mid^2 - 2 t_mid t_E + t_E^2) - t_mid^2 = -2 t_mid t_E + t_E^2 = t_E(t_E - 2 t_mid) = t_E(t_E - (t_E+t_F)) = -t_E t_F.

Thus:

4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) = |v|^2 (-t_E t_F) - 4y0^2 = -t_E t_F |v|^2 - 4y0^2.

So:

t_mid dy - őľ dx = - (t_E t_F |v|^2 + 4y0^2)/(4y0).

Thus őľ dx = t_mid dy + (t_E t_F |v|^2 + 4y0^2)/(4y0).

Hence őľ = [ t_mid dy + (t_E t_F |v|^2 + 4y0^2)/(4y0) ] / dx.

Now, we can compute O' = t_mid v + őľ n.

Now, the line ‚Ąď in translated coordinates is through H' = H - A = (dx, h_y - y0) with direction v. So ‚Ąď: X = H' + s v.

We need to show that distance from O' to ‚Ąď equals the radius R' = |O' - B'|.

The distance from O' to ‚Ąď is |(O' - H') √ó v| / |v|.

Compute O' - H' = (t_mid v + őľ n) - H' = t_mid v + őľ n - (dx, h_y - y0). But H' = (dx, h_y - y0). Note that v = (dx, dy). So:

O' - H' = (t_mid dx - dx + őľ dy, t_mid dy - (h_y - y0) - őľ dx) = ( (t_mid - 1) dx + őľ dy, t_mid dy - h_y + y0 - őľ dx).

Now, cross product (2D determinant) with v:

(O' - H') √ó v = ((t_mid - 1) dx + őľ dy) * dy - (t_mid dy - h_y + y0 - őľ dx) * dx = (t_mid - 1) dx dy + őľ dy^2 - t_mid dy dx + h_y dx - y0 dx + őľ dx^2 = (t_mid - 1 - t_mid) dx dy + őľ (dx^2+dy^2) + h_y dx - y0 dx = -dx dy + őľ |v|^2 + (h_y - y0) dx.

Thus (O' - H') √ó v = őľ |v|^2 - dx dy + (h_y - y0) dx.

Now, we also need to compute R'^2 = |O' - B'|^2 = |v|^2 (t_mid^2 + őľ^2) + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2. But we can also use the fact that O' is circumcenter, so R'^2 = |O' - E'|^2 = |v|^2 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2). This might be simpler.

Now, the tangency condition is: |(O' - H') √ó v|^2 = |v|^2 R'^2.

Thus we need to verify:

( őľ |v|^2 - dx dy + (h_y - y0) dx )^2 = |v|^2 * |v|^2 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2) = |v|^4 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2).

This is still messy. However, we have expressions for t_E, t_F, t_mid, őľ in terms of the original parameters. Perhaps we can find that the left side simplifies to |v|^4 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2) using the relations we have. Let's try to compute these expressions in terms of the original parameters.

We have:

L = |v|^2 = dx^2+dy^2.
t_E = 2r(p+r)/L.
t_F = 2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L.
t_mid = (t_E+t_F)/2 = [2r(p+r)+2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))]/(2L) = [r(p+r)+d(p-x0)]/L? Wait, compute: t_E+t_F = 2r(p+r)/L + 2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L = 2(2r(p+r)+d(p-x0))/L? Actually, t_E = 2r(p+r)/L, t_F = 2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L = 2d(p-x0)/L + 2r(p+r)/L. So t_E+t_F = 4r(p+r)/L + 2d(p-x0)/L = (4r(p+r) + 2d(p-x0))/L. Then t_mid = (2r(p+r) + d(p-x0))/L.

Thus t_mid = (2r(p+r) + d(p-x0))/L.

Now, compute t_mid - t_E = (2r(p+r)+d(p-x0))/L - 2r(p+r)/L = d(p-x0)/L.

Thus (t_mid - t_E)^2 = d^2(p-x0)^2/L^2.

Now, also we have that t_E t_F = [2r(p+r)/L] * [2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L] = 4r(p+r)(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L^2.

So t_E t_F = 4r(p+r)(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L^2.

Now, we need to compute őľ. We have:

őľ = [ t_mid dy + (t_E t_F L + 4y0^2)/(4y0) ] / dx.

Plug t_mid and t_E t_F L:

t_mid dy = dy * (2r(p+r)+d(p-x0))/L.

And t_E t_F L = 4r(p+r)(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L^2 * L = 4r(p+r)(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L.

So (t_E t_F L + 4y0^2)/(4y0) = [4r(p+r)(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L + 4y0^2]/(4y0) = [4r(p+r)(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L]/(4y0) + (4y0^2)/(4y0) = [r(p+r)(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/(y0 L)] + y0.

Thus őľ = [ dy * (2r(p+r)+d(p-x0))/L + r(p+r)(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/(y0 L) + y0 ] / dx.

Now, also note that dy = y_P - y0 = -p(x0+r)/y0 - y0 = -(p(x0+r)+y0^2)/y0 = -(p(x0+r)+r^2-x0^2)/y0 = -( (x0+r)(p+r-x0) )/y0? Actually, p(x0+r)+r^2-x0^2 = p(x0+r)+(r-x0)(r+x0) = (r+x0)(p+r-x0). So dy = -(r+x0)(p+r-x0)/y0.

And also dx = p - x0.

Now, we also have h_y = p(d-p)/y_P = p(d-p) / ( -p(x0+r)/y0 ) = - (d-p) y0/(x0+r).

Thus h_y - y0 = - (d-p) y0/(x0+r) - y0 = -y0( (d-p)/(x0+r) + 1 ) = -y0( (d-p+x0+r)/(x0+r) ). But note that x0+r =? We'll keep.

Now, we need to compute the left side of the tangency condition: ( őľ L - dx dy + (h_y - y0) dx )^2 = L^2 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2). Since L is the same as |v|^2, and (t_mid - t_E)^2 = d^2(p-x0)^2/L^2.

So we need to show:

( őľ L - dx dy + (h_y - y0) dx )^2 = L^2 ( d^2(p-x0)^2/L^2 + őľ^2 ) = d^2(p-x0)^2 + L^2 őľ^2.

Thus equivalently, we need to show that the square of őľ L - dx dy + (h_y - y0) dx equals d^2(p-x0)^2 + L^2 őľ^2.

If we denote A = őľ L - dx dy + (h_y - y0) dx, then we need A^2 = d^2(p-x0)^2 + L^2 őľ^2.

This is reminiscent of the identity: (őľ L - dx dy + (h_y - y0) dx)^2 = (őľ L + (h_y - y0) dx)^2 - 2dx dy (őľ L + (h_y - y0) dx) + (dx dy)^2? Not.

Given:

A = (x0, y0), B = (x0, -y0)

Now, compute L = |v|^2 = dx^2+dy^2.

We have:

t_E = 2r(p+r)/L
t_F = 2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L = 2d(p-x0)/L + t_E

Now, E = (x0 + t_E dx, y0 + t_E dy)
F = (x0 + t_F dx, y0 + t_F dy)

We want the circumcenter O = (o_x, o_y) of triangle BEF. Since B = (x0, -y0), E, F are on line L: A + t v. Because v = (dx, dy). So we can compute O by using the fact that the perpendicular bisector of BF and BE. But we already have a method: O = (x0+ t_mid dx, y0+ t_mid dy) + őľ n, where n = (dy, -dx). And we derived őľ = [ t_mid dy + (t_E t_F L + 4y0^2)/(4y0) ] / dx. This is messy but we can compute O explicitly.

Alternatively, we can use the formula for circumcenter in terms of coordinates: For points (x1,y1), (x2,y2), (x3,y3), the circumcenter is given by:

o_x = [ (x1^2+y1^2)(y2-y3) + (x2^2+y2^2)(y3-y1) + (x3^2+y3^2)(y1-y2) ] / [ 2(x1(y2-y3) + x2(y3-y1) + x3(y1-y2)) ]
o_y = [ (x1^2+y1^2)(x3-x2) + (x2^2+y2^2)(x1-x3) + (x3^2+y3^2)(x2-x1) ] / [ 2(x1(y2-y3) + x2(y3-y1) + x3(y1-y2)) ]

We can apply this to B=(x0,-y0), E=(x0+t_E dx, y0+t_E dy), F=(x0+t_F dx, y0+t_F dy). This might simplify because many terms have similar structure.

Let's denote:

For a point X = (x, y), define s(X) = x^2+y^2.

Then we need denominator D = 2( x_B(y_E-y_F) + x_E(y_F-y_B) + x_F(y_B-y_E) ) = 2( x_B(y_E-y_F) + x_E(y_F-y_B) + x_F(y_B-y_E) ).

Since y_E-y_F = t_E dy - t_F dy = (t_E - t_F) dy = - (t_F - t_E) dy = - (2d(p-x0)/L) dy? Actually, t_F - t_E = 2d(p-x0)/L. So y_E-y_F = - (2d(p-x0)/L) dy.

Also, y_F-y_B = (y0+t_F dy) - (-y0) = 2y0 + t_F dy.
y_B-y_E = (-y0) - (y0+t_E dy) = -2y0 - t_E dy.

Thus denominator:

D = 2[ x_B ( - (2d(p-x0)/L) dy ) + (x0+t_E dx) (2y0+t_F dy) + (x0+t_F dx) ( -2y0 - t_E dy) ].

Plug x_B = x0.

So D = 2[ - x0 * (2d(p-x0)/L) dy + (x0+t_E dx)(2y0+t_F dy) - (x0+t_F dx)(2y0+t_E dy) ].

Notice that (x0+t_E dx)(2y0+t_F dy) - (x0+t_F dx)(2y0+t_E dy) = Expand:

= x0(2y0+t_F dy) + t_E dx(2y0+t_F dy) - x0(2y0+t_E dy) - t_F dx(2y0+t_E dy) = x0(t_F dy - t_E dy) + t_E dx(2y0+t_F dy) - t_F dx(2y0+t_E dy) = x0 dy (t_F - t_E) + t_E dx 2y0 + t_E dx t_F dy - t_F dx 2y0 - t_F dx t_E dy = x0 dy (t_F - t_E) + 2y0 dx (t_E - t_F) + t_E t_F dx dy - t_E t_F dx dy = x0 dy (t_F - t_E) - 2y0 dx (t_F - t_E) = (t_F - t_E) ( x0 dy - 2y0 dx).

Thus D = 2[ - x0 * (2d(p-x0)/L) dy + (t_F - t_E) ( x0 dy - 2y0 dx) ].

But t_F - t_E = 2d(p-x0)/L. So:

D = 2[ - x0 * (2d(p-x0)/L) dy + (2d(p-x0)/L) ( x0 dy - 2y0 dx) ] = 2 * (2d(p-x0)/L) [ - x0 dy + x0 dy - 2y0 dx ] = 2 * (2d(p-x0)/L) [ -2y0 dx ] = -8y0 dx (p-x0)/L.

Thus D = -8y0 dx (p-x0)/L.

Now, note that p-x0 = dx. So D = -8y0 dx^2 / L.

Thus denominator D = -8y0 dx^2 / L.

Now, numerator for o_x: N_x = (x_B^2+y_B^2)(y_E-y_F) + (x_E^2+y_E^2)(y_F-y_B) + (x_F^2+y_F^2)(y_B-y_E).

Compute s_B = x0^2 + y0^2 = r^2.
s_E = (x0+t_E dx)^2 + (y0+t_E dy)^2 = x0^2 + 2x0 t_E dx + t_E^2 dx^2 + y0^2 + 2y0 t_E dy + t_E^2 dy^2 = r^2 + 2t_E (x0 dx + y0 dy) + t_E^2 L.
Similarly, s_F = r^2 + 2t_F (x0 dx + y0 dy) + t_F^2 L.

Now, y_E-y_F = (t_E - t_F) dy = - (t_F - t_E) dy = - (2d(p-x0)/L) dy = - (2d dx / L) dy (since p-x0=dx). So y_E-y_F = -2d dx dy / L.

y_F-y_B = (y0+t_F dy) - (-y0) = 2y0 + t_F dy.
y_B-y_E = (-y0) - (y0+t_E dy) = -2y0 - t_E dy.

Thus N_x = r^2 * (-2d dx dy / L) + s_E * (2y0+t_F dy) + s_F * (-2y0 - t_E dy).

= -2d r^2 dx dy / L + 2y0 (s_E - s_F) + dy (t_F s_E - t_E s_F).

Now, compute s_E - s_F = [r^2 + 2t_E (x0 dx + y0 dy) + t_E^2 L] - [r^2 + 2t_F (x0 dx + y0 dy) + t_F^2 L] = 2(x0 dx + y0 dy)(t_E - t_F) + L(t_E^2 - t_F^2) = 2(x0 dx + y0 dy)(- (t_F - t_E)) + L(t_E - t_F)(t_E+t_F) = - (t_F - t_E)[2(x0 dx + y0 dy) + L(t_E+t_F)].

But t_F - t_E = 2d dx / L. So:

s_E - s_F = - (2d dx / L) [ 2(x0 dx + y0 dy) + L t_mid ]? Actually, L(t_E+t_F) = L * 2 t_mid? Wait, t_E+t_F = 2 t_mid. So L(t_E+t_F) = 2L t_mid. So:

s_E - s_F = - (2d dx / L) [ 2(x0 dx + y0 dy) + 2L t_mid ] = - (2d dx / L) * 2[ x0 dx + y0 dy + L t_mid ] = -4d dx [ x0 dx + y0 dy + L t_mid ] / L.

Thus 2y0 (s_E - s_F) = -8y0 d dx [ x0 dx + y0 dy + L t_mid ] / L.

Now, compute dy (t_F s_E - t_E s_F). We have:

t_F s_E - t_E s_F = t_F (r^2 + 2t_E (x0 dx+y0 dy)+ t_E^2 L) - t_E (r^2 + 2t_F (x0 dx+y0 dy)+ t_F^2 L) = r^2 (t_F - t_E) + 2(x0 dx+y0 dy)(t_F t_E - t_E t_F) + L (t_F t_E^2 - t_E t_F^2) = r^2 (t_F - t_E) + L t_E t_F (t_E - t_F) = (t_F - t_E)(r^2 - L t_E t_F) = (2d dx / L)(r^2 - L t_E t_F).

Thus dy (t_F s_E - t_E s_F) = dy * (2d dx / L)(r^2 - L t_E t_F) = (2d dx dy / L)(r^2 - L t_E t_F).

Now, combine with the first term: -2d r^2 dx dy / L = -2d r^2 dx dy / L.

So N_x = -2d r^2 dx dy / L + (2d dx dy / L)(r^2 - L t_E t_F) - 8y0 d dx [ x0 dx + y0 dy + L t_mid ] / L.

Notice that the first two terms combine: -2d r^2 dx dy / L + (2d dx dy / L) r^2 - (2d dx dy / L) * L t_E t_F = -2d dx dy t_E t_F.

Thus N_x = -2d dx dy t_E t_F - 8y0 d dx [ x0 dx + y0 dy + L t_mid ] / L.

Now, we need to compute o_x = N_x / D = N_x / ( -8y0 dx^2 / L ) = - N_x * L / (8y0 dx^2).

So o_x = - L / (8y0 dx^2) * ( -2d dx dy t_E t_F - 8y0 d dx [ x0 dx + y0 dy + L t_mid ] / L ) = - L / (8y0 dx^2) * ( -2d dx dy t_E t_F ) - L / (8y0 dx^2) * ( -8y0 d dx [ x0 dx + y0 dy + L t_mid ] / L ) = [ L * 2d dx dy t_E t_F ] / (8y0 dx^2) + [ L * 8y0 d dx [ x0 dx + y0 dy + L t_mid ] ] / (8y0 dx^2 L) = [ 2d dy t_E t_F L ] / (8y0 dx) + [ d [ x0 dx + y0 dy + L t_mid ] ] / (dx) = [ d dy t_E t_F L ] / (4y0 dx) + [ d (x0 dx + y0 dy + L t_mid) ] / dx.

Thus o_x = d ( x0 dx + y0 dy + L t_mid ) / dx + d dy t_E t_F / (4y0 dx).

Now, note that t_mid = (t_E+t_F)/2 = [2r(p+r)/L + 2d(p-x0)/L + 2r(p+r)/L]/(2L)? Actually, we already have t_mid = (2r(p+r)+d(p-x0))/L. So L t_mid = 2r(p+r)+d(p-x0) = 2r(p+r)+d dx.

Thus x0 dx + y0 dy + L t_mid = x0 dx + y0 dy + 2r(p+r)+d dx = dx (x0+d) + y0 dy + 2r(p+r). But we might keep it.

Now, we also need o_y. The formula for o_y is:

o_y = [ s_B (x_E - x_F) + s_E (x_F - x_B) + s_F (x_B - x_E) ] / D? Actually, the standard formula: o_y = [ (x1^2+y1^2)(x3-x2) + (x2^2+y2^2)(x1-x3) + (x3^2+y3^2)(x2-x1) ] / [ 2(x1(y2-y3) + x2(y3-y1) + x3(y1-y2)) ]. We already have D = -8y0 dx^2 / L.

Now, compute x_E - x_F = (x0+t_E dx) - (x0+t_F dx) = (t_E - t_F) dx = - (t_F - t_E) dx = - (2d dx / L) dx = -2d dx^2 / L.
x_F - x_B = (x0+t_F dx) - x0 = t_F dx.
x_B - x_E = x0 - (x0+t_E dx) = -t_E dx.

Thus N_y = s_B * (-2d dx^2 / L) + s_E * (t_F dx) + s_F * (-t_E dx) = -2d s_B dx^2 / L + dx ( t_F s_E - t_E s_F ).

We already computed t_F s_E - t_E s_F = (t_F - t_E)(r^2 - L t_E t_F) = (2d dx / L)(r^2 - L t_E t_F). So:

N_y = -2d r^2 dx^2 / L + dx * (2d dx / L)(r^2 - L t_E t_F) = -2d r^2 dx^2 / L + (2d dx^2 / L)(r^2 - L t_E t_F) = -2d r^2 dx^2 / L + (2d r^2 dx^2 / L) - (2d dx^2 / L) * L t_E t_F = -2d dx^2 t_E t_F.

Thus N_y = -2d dx^2 t_E t_F.

H=(1.5,-0.3873), O_PMN=(1,-0.77475), midpoint = (1.25,-0.5810). Radius = half of circumradius = 0.6325. Circle (BEF) center (1,-1.2909), radius 0.816. Not the same.

Thus not.

There is a known property: For two intersecting circles, the circle through B and the second intersections of a line through A with the circles is orthogonal to the circle with diameter AB. Let's test that: Circle with diameter AB: center (x0,0), radius y0. We already saw that it's not orthogonal to (BEF) in numeric. But maybe it's orthogonal to the circle through B, E, F? In numeric, O_BEF = (1,-1.2909), radius 0.816. Circle with diameter AB: center (0.25,0), radius 0.9682. Distance = sqrt((0.75)^2+(-1.2909)^2)=1.493, sum of radii =1.7842, product =0.789, distance^2=2.2285, not equal. So not orthogonal.

Because the problem involves circles and circumcenters and orthocenters, coordinate geometry might be easier. Choose coordinate axes: Let M = (0,0). Let N = (d,0) with d > 0. Then circles: ő©: x^2 + y^2 = r^2. őď: (x-d)^2 + y^2 = R^2. The intersection points A and B: Solve x^2+y^2=r^2, (x-d)^2+y^2=R^2 => subtract: (x-d)^2 - x^2 = R^2 - r^2 => (x^2 -2dx+d^2) - x^2 = R^2-r^2 => -2dx+d^2 = R^2-r^2 => x = (d^2 - (R^2-r^2))/(2d) = (d^2 - R^2 + r^2)/(2d). That is the x-coordinate of the common chord (the line AB is vertical line x = constant). So let x0 = (d^2 - R^2 + r^2)/(2d). Then the y-coordinates: y = ¬Ī sqrt(r^2 - x0^2). So A and B are symmetric with respect to line MN (x-axis). Let's choose A to be the upper intersection (positive y) and B the lower intersection (negative y). Then A = (x0, y0) with y0>0, B = (x0, -y0). So A and B are symmetric across MN.

Now line MN is x-axis. The points C and D: C is on ő© and on the line MN (x-axis) such that order C, M, N, D. M = (0,0). So C is left of M on x-axis: C = (-r, 0). D is on őď and on x-axis such that D is right of N: D = (d+R, 0). Indeed, because for őď, the points on x-axis are x = d ¬Ī R. The one to the right is d+R. So D = (d+R, 0). Order: (-r,0), (0,0), (d,0), (d+R,0). So that's consistent.

Now triangle ACD: points A(x0,y0), C(-r,0), D(d+R,0). P is circumcenter of triangle ACD. So P is the intersection of perpendicular bisectors of AC and AD (or CD). Since C and D lie on x-axis, the perpendicular bisector of CD is vertical line at x = ( (-r)+(d+R) )/2 = (d+R - r)/2. So P lies on that vertical line. Also, we need to find its y-coordinate from perpendicular bisector of AC or AD. So P = ( (d+R - r)/2, y_P). We can compute y_P.

Let's compute coordinates: Let a = x0, b = y0. Then C(-r,0), D(d+R,0). Let's denote p = (d+R - r)/2. Then P = (p, y_P). The condition that P is equidistant from A and C: distance PA = PC. So (x0 - p)^2 + (y0 - y_P)^2 = ( -r - p)^2 + (0 - y_P)^2. Expand: (x0-p)^2 + y0^2 - 2 y0 y_P + y_P^2 = (p+r)^2 + y_P^2. Cancel y_P^2: (x0-p)^2 + y0^2 - 2 y0 y_P = (p+r)^2. So solve for y_P: 2 y0 y_P = (x0-p)^2 + y0^2 - (p+r)^2. So y_P = [ (x0-p)^2 + y0^2 - (p+r)^2 ]/(2 y0).

We can simplify using known relations: x0 = (d^2 - R^2 + r^2)/(2d). Also, p = (d+R - r)/2. Also, y0^2 = r^2 - x0^2. So we can compute.

The altitude from M is perpendicular to PN; from N is perpendicular to PM. But we can find H as the point such that H is the reflection of P over MN? Not exactly. For a triangle with base MN on x-axis, orthocenter lies on the line through P perpendicular to MN (i.e., vertical line x=p). So H = (p, y_H). And y_H is determined by condition that MH is perpendicular to PN, i.e., (M - H) ¬∑ (N - P) = 0. Since M = (0,0), H = (p, y_H). Then vector MH = (p, y_H). Vector PN = (d - p, 0 - y_P) = (d-p, -y_P). Dot product: p*(d-p) + y_H*(-y_P) = 0 => p(d-p) - y_H y_P = 0 => y_H = p(d-p)/y_P.

Similarly, we can also use altitude from N: (N-H) dot (M-P)=0 gives same.

So H = (p, p(d-p)/y_P). Good.

Thus v = (p - x0, -(x0+r)(p + r - x0)/y0).

A¬∑v = (x0, y0) ¬∑ (p-x0, y_P - y0) = x0(p-x0) + y0(y_P - y0) = x0(p-x0) + y0 y_P - y0^2.

But y0 y_P = y0 * (-p (x0+r)/y0) = -p (x0+r). So A¬∑v = x0(p-x0) - p(x0+r) - y0^2 = x0 p - x0^2 - p x0 - p r - y0^2 = -x0^2 - p r - y0^2 = -(x0^2+y0^2) - p r = -r^2 - p r = -r(r+p). So A¬∑v = -r(p+r). Good simplification!

Thus t_E = -2(-r(p+r))/|v|^2 = 2r(p+r)/|v|^2.

Similarly, (A-N)¬∑v: A-N = (x0-d, y0). Then (A-N)¬∑v = (x0-d)(p-x0) + y0(y_P - y0) = (x0-d)(p-x0) + y0 y_P - y0^2. y0 y_P = -p(x0+r). So (A-N)¬∑v = (x0-d)(p-x0) - p(x0+r) - y0^2 = Expand: (x0-d)(p-x0) = (x0-d)p - (x0-d)x0 = p x0 - p d - x0^2 + d x0. Then subtract p(x0+r) gives: p x0 - p d - x0^2 + d x0 - p x0 - p r = -p d - x0^2 + d x0 - p r. Then subtract y0^2: = -p d - x0^2 + d x0 - p r - (r^2 - x0^2) = -p d - x0^2 + d x0 - p r - r^2 + x0^2 = -p d + d x0 - p r - r^2 = d(x0 - p) - r(p+r). But x0-p = -(p-x0). So d(x0-p) = -d(p-x0). So (A-N)¬∑v = -d(p-x0) - r(p+r). So (A-N)¬∑v = -[d(p-x0) + r(p+r)]. Then t_F = -2((A-N)¬∑v)/|v|^2 = -2(-[d(p-x0) + r(p+r)])/|v|^2 = 2(d(p-x0) + r(p+r))/|v|^2.

Thus we have:

E = A + (2r(p+r)/|v|^2) v
F = A + (2(d(p-x0) + r(p+r))/|v|^2) v

Given the time, I think it's more feasible to produce a coordinate proof in the MN as x-axis system, but we need to simplify the algebra. Let's denote:

Let‚Äôs use the following notations to reduce clutter:

Let r, R, d, x0, y0 be as defined.
Let p = (d+R-r)/2.
Let L = |v|^2 = (p-x0)^2 + (y_P - y0)^2. We have y_P = -p (x0+r)/y0.
Thus we can compute L.

Also, let t_E = 2r(p+r)/L, t_F = 2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L.
Note that t_F = 2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L = 2(d(p-x0))/L + t_E.

We also have B = (x0, -y0), E = A + t_E v, F = A + t_F v.

Now, we can compute the circumcenter O of triangle BEF. Since E and F are on line L: A + t v, and B is symmetric to A across x-axis, maybe we can find a formula for O in terms of A, v, and B. Let's try to compute O using the fact that O is the intersection of perpendicular bisector of EF and perpendicular bisector of BF (or BE). Since E and F are on line L, the perpendicular bisector of EF is the line perpendicular to v through the midpoint of EF. That midpoint is M_EF = A + (t_E+t_F)/2 v = A + t_mid v, where t_mid = (t_E+t_F)/2. So O = A + t_mid v + őľ n, where n = (dy, -dx) is a unit vector perpendicular to v (since dot with v = 0). So O = A + t_mid v + őľ n.

Now, O must also satisfy that distance to B equals distance to E (or F). Since O is on perpendicular bisector of EF, we have OE = OF. So we only need OB = OE. So:

|O - B|^2 = |O - E|^2.

Compute O - B = (A + t_mid v + őľ n) - B = (A - B) + t_mid v + őľ n.
But A - B = (x0 - x0, y0 - (-y0)) = (0, 2y0). So A-B = (0, 2y0).

Thus O-B = (0, 2y0) + t_mid v + őľ n.

Similarly, O-E = (A + t_mid v + őľ n) - (A + t_E v) = (t_mid - t_E) v + őľ n.

Now, v = (dx, dy), n = (dy, -dx) (since n is perpendicular to v, but note that |v|^2 = dx^2+dy^2, and n has same length? Actually, if we take n = (dy, -dx), then |n|^2 = dy^2+dx^2 = |v|^2, so n is not unit; it has length |v|. But that's fine; we can incorporate that.

We have:

|O-B|^2 = |(0,2y0) + t_mid v + őľ n|^2 = |(0,2y0) + t_mid v|^2 + őľ^2 |n|^2 + 2őľ ( (0,2y0)+ t_mid v )¬∑ n.
|O-E|^2 = |(t_mid - t_E) v + őľ n|^2 = (t_mid - t_E)^2 |v|^2 + őľ^2 |v|^2 + 2őľ (t_mid - t_E) v¬∑n. But v¬∑n = dx*dy + dy*(-dx)=0. So |O-E|^2 = |v|^2 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2).

Set them equal:

|(0,2y0) + t_mid v|^2 + őľ^2 |v|^2 + 2őľ ( (0,2y0)+ t_mid v )¬∑ n = |v|^2 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2).

Cancel őľ^2 |v|^2 both sides:

|(0,2y0) + t_mid v|^2 + 2őľ ( (0,2y0)+ t_mid v )¬∑ n = |v|^2 (t_mid - t_E)^2.

Thus we can solve for őľ:

2őľ ( (0,2y0)+ t_mid v )¬∑ n = |v|^2 (t_mid - t_E)^2 - |(0,2y0) + t_mid v|^2.

Now, compute the left side dot product:

Given the complexity, I think the coordinate proof is the way to go, but we need to present it clearly, with careful algebraic simplifications. Since the problem is from an olympiad, a coordinate solution is acceptable if done rigorously. Let's attempt to produce a clean coordinate proof.

We set up coordinates:

Let M = (0,0), N = (d,0) with d > 0. Let ő©: x^2 + y^2 = r^2, őď: (x-d)^2 + y^2 = R^2, with r < R and |R-r| < d < R+r. The circles intersect at A and B. By symmetry, we can choose A = (x0, y0) with y0 > 0, B = (x0, -y0), where x0 = (d^2 - R^2 + r^2)/(2d), y0 = sqrt(r^2 - x0^2) > 0.

Now, the line MN is the x-axis. It meets ő© at C = (-r,0) and őď at D = (d+R,0), with order C, M, N, D. So C = (-r,0), D = (d+R,0).

Now, define P as circumcenter of triangle ACD. Since C and D lie on x-axis, the perpendicular bisector of CD is vertical line x = (C_x + D_x)/2 = ( -r + d+R )/2 = (d+R-r)/2 = p. So P has x-coordinate p. Let P = (p, y_P). Since PA = PC, we have (x0-p)^2 + (y0-y_P)^2 = (-r-p)^2 + y_P^2. Expanding gives -2x0p + x0^2 + y0^2 -2y0y_P + y_P^2 = p^2 + 2pr + r^2 + y_P^2. Cancel y_P^2 and use x0^2+y0^2 = r^2. Then we get -2x0p + r^2 -2y0y_P = p^2 + 2pr + r^2 => -2x0p -2y0y_P = p^2 + 2pr => 2y0y_P = -p^2 -2pr -2x0p = -p(p+2r+2x0). So y_P = -p(p+2r+2x0)/(2y0). But we earlier found y_P = -p(x0+r)/y0. Let's check consistency: p(p+2r+2x0)/(2y0) = p(p+2r+2x0)/(2y0). Is that equal to p(x0+r)/y0? That would require p+2r+2x0 = 2(x0+r) => p+2r+2x0 = 2x0+2r => p=0, which is not. So there is a discrepancy. Let's re-derive carefully.

We have C = (-r, 0), D = (d+R, 0). Their midpoint: x = (-r + d+R)/2 = p. So perpendicular bisector of CD: x = p. So P = (p, y_P). Now, condition PA = PC: distance from P to A equals distance from P to C.

PA^2 = (x0-p)^2 + (y0-y_P)^2.
PC^2 = (-r-p)^2 + (0-y_P)^2 = (p+r)^2 + y_P^2. (since -r-p = -(p+r), square = (p+r)^2).

Set equal:

(x0-p)^2 + y0^2 - 2y0 y_P + y_P^2 = (p+r)^2 + y_P^2.

Cancel y_P^2:

(x0-p)^2 + y0^2 - 2y0 y_P = (p+r)^2.

Now, (x0-p)^2 = x0^2 - 2x0p + p^2. So:

x0^2 - 2x0p + p^2 + y0^2 - 2y0 y_P = p^2 + 2pr + r^2.

Cancel p^2:

x0^2 + y0^2 - 2x0p - 2y0 y_P = 2pr + r^2.

But x0^2+y0^2 = r^2. So:

r^2 - 2x0p - 2y0 y_P = 2pr + r^2 => -2x0p - 2y0 y_P = 2pr => Divide 2: -x0p - y0 y_P = pr => Thus y0 y_P = -pr - x0p = -p(r+x0). So y_P = -p(r+x0)/y0.

That matches our earlier expression. Good. So we have y_P = -p (r+x0)/y0.

Now, note that r+x0 > 0 because x0 ‚Č• -r, and if x0 = -r then A is at (-r,y0) with y0=0? Actually if x0=-r, then y0^2 = r^2 - r^2 =0, so A = (-r,0)=C, which would be degenerate. So x0 > -r, so r+x0 >0. So y_P <0.

Now, line AP: through A(x0,y0) and P(p, y_P). Its direction vector v = (p-x0, y_P-y0). We'll keep it.

Now, let's find E and F as second intersections of line AP with ő© and őď.

Parameterize line AP: X(t) = A + t v, t real. For t=0: A; t=1: P. For ő©: |X(t)|^2 = r^2. Since |A|^2 = r^2, we have |A + t v|^2 = r^2 + 2t (A¬∑v) + t^2 |v|^2 = r^2 => 2t (A¬∑v) + t^2 |v|^2 = 0 => t(2A¬∑v + t|v|^2)=0. Non-zero root: t_E = -2(A¬∑v)/|v|^2. Similarly, for őď: (X(t)-N)^2 = R^2. N=(d,0). So (A+N? Actually, (A - N + t v)^2 = R^2. Since |A-N|^2 = R^2, we get 2t ( (A-N)¬∑v ) + t^2 |v|^2 = 0 => t_F = -2((A-N)¬∑v)/|v|^2. So t_E and t_F as given.

Another approach: Use coordinates but with a more clever parameterization. Let‚Äôs set up coordinates with A at origin, and let the line AP be the x-axis. Then we have M = (őĪ,ő≤), N = (ő≥,őī). The circles: x^2+y^2 = 2őĪ x + 2ő≤ y and x^2+y^2 = 2ő≥ x + 2őī y. The points E and F are on x-axis: E=(2őĪ,0), F=(2ő≥,0). The point B is the other intersection of the circles. We can compute B coordinates in terms of őĪ,ő≤,ő≥,őī. Then we need to compute H, orthocenter of triangle PMN, with P=(p,0) on x-axis. And then show that the horizontal line through H is tangent to circle through B, E, F.

Now, we have the relation that P is circumcenter of triangle ACD. In this coordinate system, A=0, P=(p,0). And we have C and D are points on line MN (centers) and on circles. We can compute C and D in terms of M,N. The condition that P is circumcenter gives:

p C_x = |C|^2/2, p D_x = |D|^2/2.

Thus we have two equations that determine p and also give a relation between M,N. So we can solve for p.

Now, we can also compute H: orthocenter of triangle PMN. Since M=(őĪ,ő≤), N=(ő≥,őī), P=(p,0). The orthocenter H can be computed using the formula: H = M + N + P - 2 O, where O is circumcenter of triangle PMN. But we can also compute H directly as intersection of altitudes. Since P is on x-axis, altitude from P is perpendicular to MN. So H lies on line through P perpendicular to MN. That line is given by: (x,y) = (p,0) + u (őī-ő≤, -(ő≥-őĪ))? Actually, direction vector perpendicular to MN = (ő≥-őĪ, őī-ő≤) is (őī-ő≤, -(ő≥-őĪ)). So line: (p + u(őī-ő≤), -u(ő≥-őĪ)). So H = (p + u_H (őī-ő≤), -u_H (ő≥-őĪ)). Now, also H must lie on altitude from M, which is perpendicular to PN. PN vector: N-P = (ő≥-p, őī). So altitude from M: through M, direction perpendicular to PN: (őī, -(ő≥-p)). So line: (őĪ,ő≤) + s (őī, -(ő≥-p)). The intersection gives equations.

Alternatively, we can compute y_H = -u_H (ő≥-őĪ). So we need u_H.

Now, we also have B = (x_B, y_B) from earlier: B = t (v, -u) with u = őĪ-ő≥, v = ő≤-őī, t = 2(őĪ v - ő≤ u)/L^2, where L^2 = u^2+v^2.

Now, the circle (BEF): E=(2őĪ,0), F=(2ő≥,0), B=(x_B,y_B). Its circumcenter O = (őĪ+ő≥, o_y) because perpendicular bisector of EF is vertical x = őĪ+ő≥. So O_x = őĪ+ő≥. And radius R = distance from O to E = sqrt((őĪ+ő≥-2őĪ)^2 + o_y^2) = sqrt((ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2). Also, OB = R gives:

(őĪ+ő≥ - x_B)^2 + (o_y - y_B)^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2.

Simplify:

(őĪ+ő≥ - x_B)^2 + o_y^2 - 2 o_y y_B + y_B^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2

=> (őĪ+ő≥ - x_B)^2 - 2 o_y y_B + y_B^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2

=> 2 o_y y_B = (őĪ+ő≥ - x_B)^2 + y_B^2 - (ő≥-őĪ)^2

=> o_y = [ (őĪ+ő≥ - x_B)^2 + y_B^2 - (ő≥-őĪ)^2 ] / (2 y_B), assuming y_B ‚Č† 0.

Now, the horizontal line through H is y = y_H. For it to be tangent to circle (BEF), we need |y_H - o_y| = R = sqrt((ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2). This is equivalent to (y_H - o_y)^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2 => y_H^2 - 2 y_H o_y + o_y^2 = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 + o_y^2 => y_H^2 - 2 y_H o_y = (ő≥-őĪ)^2 => 2 y_H o_y = y_H^2 - (ő≥-őĪ)^2 => o_y = (y_H^2 - (ő≥-őĪ)^2)/(2 y_H). So we need to verify that the expression for o_y from B satisfies this.

Thus we need to compute y_H and then check that the o_y computed from B satisfies that relation. So we need to compute p and y_H in terms of őĪ,ő≤,ő≥,őī. Then compute B in terms of őĪ,ő≤,ő≥,őī. Then compute o_y and then show that o_y = (y_H^2 - (ő≥-őĪ)^2)/(2 y_H). That is an algebraic identity.

Let's attempt to derive p from the condition that P is circumcenter of ACD.

In the A=0, AP=x-axis system, we have A=0, P=(p,0). The points C and D are on line MN (through M and N). Let's compute M and N coordinates. We have:

M = (őĪ,ő≤)
N = (ő≥,őī)

Define d = N-M = (ő≥-őĪ, őī-ő≤). L = |d|.

Now, C = M - (r/L) d, where r = |M| = sqrt(őĪ^2+ő≤^2).
D = M + (1+R/L) d, where R = |N| = sqrt(ő≥^2+őī^2).

Now, condition P is circumcenter of ACD. Since A=0, we have:

P¬∑C = |C|^2/2  => p C_x = |C|^2/2
P¬∑D = |D|^2/2  => p D_x = |D|^2/2

Thus we have:

C_x = |C|^2/(2p)
D_x = |D|^2/(2p)

Now, compute C_x and |C|^2. As before:

|C|^2 = 2r^2 - (2r/L) M¬∑d, and M¬∑d = (R^2 - r^2 - L^2)/2.
So |C|^2 = 2r^2 - (2r/L)*((R^2 - r^2 - L^2)/2) = 2r^2 - (r/L)(R^2 - r^2 - L^2) = 2r^2 - (rR^2)/L + (r^3)/L + rL.

Also, C_x = őĪ - (r/L)(ő≥-őĪ) = őĪ - (r/L)(ő≥-őĪ).

Thus p = |C|^2/(2C_x). So p = [2r^2 - (rR^2)/L + (r^3)/L + rL] / [2(őĪ - (r/L)(ő≥-őĪ))].

This is still messy. But perhaps we can find a simpler expression for p by using the fact that P is also the circumcenter of triangle ACD, so it is the center of the circle through A, C, D. In complex numbers, if A=0, then the circumcenter is given by (c d (cŐĄ - dŐĄ))/(c dŐĄ - cŐĄ d). So p = (c d (cŐĄ - dŐĄ))/(c dŐĄ - cŐĄ d). Since p is real (on x-axis), this gives a condition.

Define v = (dx, dy) = (p-x0, y_P-y0)

We have t_E = 2r(p+r)/L, t_F = 2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L, where L = dx^2+dy^2.

Now, E = A + t_E v, F = A + t_F v.

We want to find the circumcenter O of triangle BEF. Since B = (x0, -y0), E = (x0 + t_E dx, y0 + t_E dy), F = (x0 + t_F dx, y0 + t_F dy). Let‚Äôs denote:

A' = (0,0)
B' = B - A = (0, -2y0)
E' = E - A = (t_E dx, t_E dy)
F' = F - A = (t_F dx, t_F dy)

Now, we have points: A'=0, B'=(0, -2y0), E'=(t_E dx, t_E dy), F'=(t_F dx, t_F dy). This is similar to the A=0 system we had earlier, but with B' on y-axis, and the line AP becomes the line through origin with direction v. Let‚Äôs denote:

Now, the circumcenter O' of triangle BEF. Since E and F lie on line through origin with direction v, the perpendicular bisector of EF is the line through the midpoint of EF, perpendicular to v. That midpoint is M_EF = ((a+b)/2 dx, (a+b)/2 dy) = t_mid v, where t_mid = (a+b)/2. The direction perpendicular to v is n = (dy, -dx). So O' = t_mid v + őľ n for some őľ.

Now, O' must satisfy that distance to B equals distance to E (or F). So |O' - B|^2 = |O' - E|^2.

Compute O' - B = t_mid v + őľ n - (0, -2y0) = t_mid v + őľ n + (0, 2y0) (since minus B gives + (0, 2y0)? Actually, B = (0, -2y0), so O' - B = (t_mid dx + őľ dy, t_mid dy - őľ dx) - (0, -2y0) = (t_mid dx + őľ dy, t_mid dy - őľ dx + 2y0). And O' - E = (t_mid v + őľ n) - (a v) = (t_mid - a) v + őľ n.

Now, as before, v¬∑n=0. So |O'-E|^2 = (t_mid - a)^2 |v|^2 + őľ^2 |v|^2 = |v|^2 ((t_mid - a)^2 + őľ^2).

And |O'-B|^2 = |(t_mid dx + őľ dy, t_mid dy - őľ dx + 2y0)|^2 = (t_mid dx + őľ dy)^2 + (t_mid dy - őľ dx + 2y0)^2.

Expand:

= t_mid^2 dx^2 + 2 t_mid dx őľ dy + őľ^2 dy^2 + (t_mid dy - őľ dx)^2 + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2

= |v|^2 (t_mid^2 + őľ^2) + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2.

Set equal to |v|^2 ((t_mid - a)^2 + őľ^2). Cancel őľ^2 |v|^2:

|v|^2 t_mid^2 + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2 = |v|^2 (t_mid - a)^2.

Thus:

4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) = |v|^2 ((t_mid - a)^2 - t_mid^2) - 4y0^2.

Compute ((t_mid - a)^2 - t_mid^2) = (t_mid^2 - 2t_mid a + a^2) - t_mid^2 = -2t_mid a + a^2 = a(a - 2t_mid). But note that a = t_E, and t_mid = (a+b)/2, so a - 2t_mid = a - (a+b) = -b. So ((t_mid - a)^2 - t_mid^2) = a(-b) = -a b.

Thus:

4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) = |v|^2 (-a b) - 4y0^2 = -ab |v|^2 - 4y0^2.

So:

4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) = -ab |v|^2 - 4y0^2.

Thus:

Now, we can solve for őľ:

őľ dx = t_mid dy + (ab |v|^2 + 4y0^2)/(4y0).

Given the difficulty, I think the coordinate approach with the MN as x-axis system and using vector algebra to verify the identity is doable if we keep expressions and use the relations we have. Let's attempt to compute the condition using the fact that the line ‚Ąď is tangent to circle (BEF) iff the equation for the intersection of ‚Ąď and the circle has discriminant zero. That is:

| (H - O) + s v |^2 = R^2.

We can compute the discriminant in terms of the dot products. The discriminant őĒ = 4[ (H-O)¬∑v ]^2 - 4|v|^2 (|H-O|^2 - R^2) = 0 => [ (H-O)¬∑v ]^2 = |v|^2 (|H-O|^2 - R^2).

Now, we can compute H-O and R. We have O = circumcenter of BEF. In the translated system with A=0, we have O' = t_mid v + őľ n. And H' = H - A = (dx, y_H - y0). And we have B' = (0, -2y0). Also, we have expressions for t_mid, őľ, etc. So we need to compute O' - H' and then the dot product with v.

Given that we have explicit formulas for t_mid and őľ, we can compute (H'-O')¬∑v = - (O'-H')¬∑v. So we need (O'-H')¬∑v. But O' = t_mid v + őľ n, so (O'-H')¬∑v = t_mid |v|^2 + őľ (n¬∑v) - H'¬∑v. Since n¬∑v=0, we get = t_mid |v|^2 - H'¬∑v. Thus (H'-O')¬∑v = -t_mid |v|^2 + H'¬∑v.

Now, compute H'¬∑v = (dx, y_H - y0)¬∑(dx, dy) = dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy = dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy.

Thus (H'-O')¬∑v = -t_mid |v|^2 + dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy.

Now, we also need |H'-O'|^2 - R^2. R^2 = |O'-B'|^2 = |(t_mid v + őľ n) - (0, -2y0)|^2 = |t_mid v + őľ n + (0, 2y0)|^2. As before, |O'-B'|^2 = |v|^2 (t_mid^2+őľ^2) + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2. But we also have that O' is the circumcenter, so OB' = OE' = etc. But we can compute |H'-O'|^2 - R^2 = |(H'-O')|^2 - |O'-B'|^2.

We can compute (H'-O') = H' - (t_mid v + őľ n) = (H' - t_mid v) - őľ n.

Then |H'-O'|^2 = |H' - t_mid v|^2 + őľ^2 |n|^2 - 2őľ (H' - t_mid v)¬∑ n.

Since n¬∑v=0, we have H'¬∑n =? H' = (dx, y_H - y0). n = (dy, -dx). So H'¬∑n = dx dy + (y_H - y0)(-dx) = dx dy - dx(y_H - y0) = dx (dy - y_H + y0). Also, t_mid v¬∑n =0. So (H' - t_mid v)¬∑ n = H'¬∑n.

Thus |H'-O'|^2 = |H' - t_mid v|^2 + őľ^2 |v|^2 - 2őľ H'¬∑n.

Now, |H' - t_mid v|^2 = |H'|^2 + t_mid^2 |v|^2 - 2 t_mid H'¬∑v.

So |H'-O'|^2 = |H'|^2 + t_mid^2 |v|^2 - 2 t_mid H'¬∑v + őľ^2 |v|^2 - 2őľ H'¬∑n.

Then |H'-O'|^2 - R^2 = [|H'|^2 + t_mid^2 |v|^2 - 2 t_mid H'¬∑v + őľ^2 |v|^2 - 2őľ H'¬∑n] - [|v|^2 (t_mid^2+őľ^2) + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2] = |H'|^2 - 2 t_mid H'¬∑v - 2őľ H'¬∑n - 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) - 4y0^2.

Simplify: |H'|^2 = dx^2 + (y_H - y0)^2.

And H'¬∑v = dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy.

Thus -2 t_mid H'¬∑v = -2 t_mid (dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy). So the expression becomes:

|H'|^2 - 2 t_mid H'¬∑v - 2őľ H'¬∑n - 4y0 t_mid dy + 4y0 őľ dx - 4y0^2.

= |H'|^2 - 2 t_mid (dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy) - 2őľ H'¬∑n - 4y0 t_mid dy + 4y0 őľ dx - 4y0^2.

Now, |H'|^2 = dx^2 + (y_H - y0)^2. So combine with -2 t_mid dx^2: = dx^2 (1-2t_mid) + (y_H - y0)^2 - 2 t_mid (y_H - y0) dy - 2őľ H'¬∑n - 4y0 t_mid dy + 4y0 őľ dx - 4y0^2.

Thus |H'-O'|^2 - R^2 = dx^2 (1-2t_mid) + (y_H - y0)^2 - 2 t_mid (y_H - y0) dy - 2őľ H'¬∑n - 4y0 t_mid dy + 4y0 őľ dx - 4y0^2.

Now, we also need the left side of the tangency condition: [ (H'-O')¬∑v ]^2 = |v|^2 (|H'-O'|^2 - R^2). But we already have (H'-O')¬∑v = -t_mid |v|^2 + H'¬∑v = -t_mid L + (dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy), where L = |v|^2.

So (H'-O')¬∑v = -t_mid L + dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy.

Thus we need to verify:

(-t_mid L + dx^2 + (y_H - y0) dy)^2 = L ( |H'-O'|^2 - R^2 ).

That is a messy equation. However, we have explicit expressions for t_mid and őľ in terms of a,b, etc. And we have a,b = t_E, t_F. So we can plug in.

I'll define:

Let M = (0,0), N = (d,0) with d > 0. Let r = |M A|? Actually, we have ő©: x^2+y^2 = r^2, őď: (x-d)^2+y^2 = R^2, with r < R and |R-r| < d < R+r. Let A = (x0, y0) with y0 > 0, B = (x0, -y0). Then x0 = (d^2 - R^2 + r^2)/(2d), y0 = sqrt(r^2 - x0^2) > 0.

Define p = (d+R-r)/2, so that C = (-r,0), D = (d+R,0) and the perpendicular bisector of CD is x = p.

Now, P is the circumcenter of triangle ACD. Since C and D lie on x-axis, the perpendicular bisector of CD is x = p, so P has x-coordinate p. Let P = (p, y_P). From PA = PC, we have (x0-p)^2 + (y0-y_P)^2 = (p+r)^2 + y_P^2. Expanding gives (x0-p)^2 + y0^2 - 2y0y_P + y_P^2 = p^2+2pr+r^2+y_P^2. Using x0^2+y0^2 = r^2, we get -2x0p + r^2 -2y0y_P = 2pr + r^2 => -2x0p -2y0y_P = 2pr => y0y_P = -p(x0+r) => y_P = -p(x0+r)/y0.

Thus P = (p, -p(x0+r)/y0).

Now, line AP: direction v = (p-x0, y_P - y0). We'll denote v = (dx, dy). Then t_E = 2r(p+r)/|v|^2, t_F = 2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/|v|^2. So E = A + t_E v, F = A + t_F v.

Now, H is orthocenter of triangle PMN. M=(0,0), N=(d,0), P=(p, y_P). The altitude from P is vertical line x=p. The altitude from M is perpendicular to PN. PN vector = (d-p, -y_P). A direction vector perpendicular to PN is (y_P, d-p). So altitude from M: parametric (0,0)+s(y_P, d-p). Setting x = p gives s = p/y_P. Then y = s(d-p) = p(d-p)/y_P. Thus H = (p, p(d-p)/y_P). Since y_P < 0, we have H_y = p(d-p)/y_P < 0. So H = (p, h_y) with h_y = p(d-p)/y_P.

Now, we need to prove that the line ‚Ąď through H parallel to v is tangent to the circumcircle of triangle BEF.

We will compute the circumcircle of BEF. Let‚Äôs denote:

B = (x0, -y0)
E = (x0 + t_E dx, y0 + t_E dy)
F = (x0 + t_F dx, y0 + t_F dy)

We'll find the circumcenter O of triangle BEF. Since E and F lie on the line L through A with direction v, and B is the reflection of A across the x-axis, we can use the following approach: Consider the translation that sends A to the origin. Define new coordinates:

Let X' = X - A. Then:

A' = (0,0)
B' = (0, -2y0)
E' = (t_E dx, t_E dy)
F' = (t_F dx, t_F dy)

Now, we need to find the circumcenter O' of triangle B'E'F'. Since B' is on the y-axis, and E',F' are on the line through origin with direction v, the perpendicular bisector of E'F' is the line through the midpoint of E'F' perpendicular to v. Let‚Äôs denote:

t_mid = (t_E + t_F)/2.
M_EF = t_mid v = (t_mid dx, t_mid dy).
Let n = (dy, -dx), which is perpendicular to v. Then O' = t_mid v + őľ n for some őľ.

Now, O' must satisfy that |O' - B'|^2 = |O' - E'|^2. We can solve for őľ.

Compute:

|O' - E'|^2 = | (t_mid - t_E) v + őľ n |^2 = (t_mid - t_E)^2 |v|^2 + őľ^2 |v|^2 (since v¬∑n=0). So = |v|^2 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2).

Now, |O' - B'|^2 = | t_mid v + őľ n - (0, -2y0) |^2 = | t_mid v + őľ n + (0, 2y0) |^2 = (t_mid dx + őľ dy)^2 + (t_mid dy - őľ dx + 2y0)^2.

Expand:

= t_mid^2 dx^2 + 2 t_mid dx őľ dy + őľ^2 dy^2 + (t_mid dy - őľ dx)^2 + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2

= t_mid^2 (dx^2+dy^2) + őľ^2 (dx^2+dy^2) + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2

= |v|^2 (t_mid^2 + őľ^2) + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2.

Set equal to |v|^2 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2). Cancel őľ^2 |v|^2:

|v|^2 t_mid^2 + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2 = |v|^2 (t_mid - t_E)^2.

Thus:

4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) = |v|^2 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 - t_mid^2) - 4y0^2.

Compute ((t_mid - t_E)^2 - t_mid^2) = (t_mid^2 - 2 t_mid t_E + t_E^2) - t_mid^2 = -2 t_mid t_E + t_E^2 = t_E(t_E - 2 t_mid) = t_E(t_E - (t_E+t_F)) = -t_E t_F.

Thus:

4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) = |v|^2 (-t_E t_F) - 4y0^2 = -t_E t_F |v|^2 - 4y0^2.

So:

t_mid dy - őľ dx = - (t_E t_F |v|^2 + 4y0^2)/(4y0).

Thus őľ dx = t_mid dy + (t_E t_F |v|^2 + 4y0^2)/(4y0).

Hence őľ = [ t_mid dy + (t_E t_F |v|^2 + 4y0^2)/(4y0) ] / dx.

Now, we can compute O' = t_mid v + őľ n.

Now, the line ‚Ąď in translated coordinates is through H' = H - A = (dx, h_y - y0) with direction v. So ‚Ąď: X = H' + s v.

We need to show that distance from O' to ‚Ąď equals the radius R' = |O' - B'|.

The distance from O' to ‚Ąď is |(O' - H') √ó v| / |v|.

Compute O' - H' = (t_mid v + őľ n) - H' = t_mid v + őľ n - (dx, h_y - y0). But H' = (dx, h_y - y0). Note that v = (dx, dy). So:

O' - H' = (t_mid dx - dx + őľ dy, t_mid dy - (h_y - y0) - őľ dx) = ( (t_mid - 1) dx + őľ dy, t_mid dy - h_y + y0 - őľ dx).

Now, cross product (2D determinant) with v:

(O' - H') √ó v = ((t_mid - 1) dx + őľ dy) * dy - (t_mid dy - h_y + y0 - őľ dx) * dx = (t_mid - 1) dx dy + őľ dy^2 - t_mid dy dx + h_y dx - y0 dx + őľ dx^2 = (t_mid - 1 - t_mid) dx dy + őľ (dx^2+dy^2) + h_y dx - y0 dx = -dx dy + őľ |v|^2 + (h_y - y0) dx.

Thus (O' - H') √ó v = őľ |v|^2 - dx dy + (h_y - y0) dx.

Now, we also need to compute R'^2 = |O' - B'|^2 = |v|^2 (t_mid^2 + őľ^2) + 4y0(t_mid dy - őľ dx) + 4y0^2. But we can also use the fact that O' is circumcenter, so R'^2 = |O' - E'|^2 = |v|^2 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2). This might be simpler.

Now, the tangency condition is: |(O' - H') √ó v|^2 = |v|^2 R'^2.

Thus we need to verify:

( őľ |v|^2 - dx dy + (h_y - y0) dx )^2 = |v|^2 * |v|^2 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2) = |v|^4 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2).

This is still messy. However, we have expressions for t_E, t_F, t_mid, őľ in terms of the original parameters. Perhaps we can find that the left side simplifies to |v|^4 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2) using the relations we have. Let's try to compute these expressions in terms of the original parameters.

We have:

L = |v|^2 = dx^2+dy^2.
t_E = 2r(p+r)/L.
t_F = 2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L.
t_mid = (t_E+t_F)/2 = [2r(p+r)+2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))]/(2L) = [r(p+r)+d(p-x0)]/L? Wait, compute: t_E+t_F = 2r(p+r)/L + 2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L = 2(2r(p+r)+d(p-x0))/L? Actually, t_E = 2r(p+r)/L, t_F = 2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L = 2d(p-x0)/L + 2r(p+r)/L. So t_E+t_F = 4r(p+r)/L + 2d(p-x0)/L = (4r(p+r) + 2d(p-x0))/L. Then t_mid = (2r(p+r) + d(p-x0))/L.

Thus t_mid = (2r(p+r) + d(p-x0))/L.

Now, compute t_mid - t_E = (2r(p+r)+d(p-x0))/L - 2r(p+r)/L = d(p-x0)/L.

Thus (t_mid - t_E)^2 = d^2(p-x0)^2/L^2.

Now, also we have that t_E t_F = [2r(p+r)/L] * [2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L] = 4r(p+r)(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L^2.

So t_E t_F = 4r(p+r)(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L^2.

Now, we need to compute őľ. We have:

őľ = [ t_mid dy + (t_E t_F L + 4y0^2)/(4y0) ] / dx.

Plug t_mid and t_E t_F L:

t_mid dy = dy * (2r(p+r)+d(p-x0))/L.

And t_E t_F L = 4r(p+r)(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L^2 * L = 4r(p+r)(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L.

So (t_E t_F L + 4y0^2)/(4y0) = [4r(p+r)(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L + 4y0^2]/(4y0) = [4r(p+r)(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L]/(4y0) + (4y0^2)/(4y0) = [r(p+r)(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/(y0 L)] + y0.

Thus őľ = [ dy * (2r(p+r)+d(p-x0))/L + r(p+r)(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/(y0 L) + y0 ] / dx.

Now, also note that dy = y_P - y0 = -p(x0+r)/y0 - y0 = -(p(x0+r)+y0^2)/y0 = -(p(x0+r)+r^2-x0^2)/y0 = -( (x0+r)(p+r-x0) )/y0? Actually, p(x0+r)+r^2-x0^2 = p(x0+r)+(r-x0)(r+x0) = (r+x0)(p+r-x0). So dy = -(r+x0)(p+r-x0)/y0.

And also dx = p - x0.

Now, we also have h_y = p(d-p)/y_P = p(d-p) / ( -p(x0+r)/y0 ) = - (d-p) y0/(x0+r).

Thus h_y - y0 = - (d-p) y0/(x0+r) - y0 = -y0( (d-p)/(x0+r) + 1 ) = -y0( (d-p+x0+r)/(x0+r) ). But note that x0+r =? We'll keep.

Now, we need to compute the left side of the tangency condition: ( őľ L - dx dy + (h_y - y0) dx )^2 = L^2 ((t_mid - t_E)^2 + őľ^2). Since L is the same as |v|^2, and (t_mid - t_E)^2 = d^2(p-x0)^2/L^2.

So we need to show:

( őľ L - dx dy + (h_y - y0) dx )^2 = L^2 ( d^2(p-x0)^2/L^2 + őľ^2 ) = d^2(p-x0)^2 + L^2 őľ^2.

Thus equivalently, we need to show that the square of őľ L - dx dy + (h_y - y0) dx equals d^2(p-x0)^2 + L^2 őľ^2.

If we denote A = őľ L - dx dy + (h_y - y0) dx, then we need A^2 = d^2(p-x0)^2 + L^2 őľ^2.

This is reminiscent of the identity: (őľ L - dx dy + (h_y - y0) dx)^2 = (őľ L + (h_y - y0) dx)^2 - 2dx dy (őľ L + (h_y - y0) dx) + (dx dy)^2? Not.

Given the time, I'll attempt to write a coordinate proof that is clear and rigorous, using the MN as x-axis system. I'll compute the circumcenter O of triangle BEF using the determinant formula. Then I'll compute the distance from O to line ‚Ąď and the radius R. Then I'll verify the equality using the relations we have. Let's do it systematically.

Given:

M = (0,0), N = (d,0)
A = (x0, y0), B = (x0, -y0)
C = (-r,0), D = (d+R,0)
p = (d+R-r)/2
y_P = -p(x0+r)/y0
dx = p-x0, dy = y_P - y0 = -p(x0+r)/y0 - y0 = -(p(x0+r)+y0^2)/y0 = -(p(x0+r)+r^2-x0^2)/y0 = -( (x0+r)(p+r-x0) )/y0? Actually, p(x0+r)+r^2-x0^2 = p(x0+r)+(r-x0)(r+x0) = (r+x0)(p+r-x0). So dy = -(r+x0)(p+r-x0)/y0.

Now, compute L = |v|^2 = dx^2+dy^2.

We have:

t_E = 2r(p+r)/L
t_F = 2(d(p-x0)+r(p+r))/L = 2d(p-x0)/L + t_E

Now, E = (x0 + t_E dx, y0 + t_E dy)
F = (x0 + t_F dx, y0 + t_F dy)

We want the circumcenter O = (o_x, o_y) of triangle BEF. Since B = (x0, -y0), E, F are on line L: A + t v. Because v = (dx, dy). So we can compute O by using the fact that the perpendicular bisector of BF and BE. But we already have a method: O = (x0+ t_mid dx, y0+ t_mid dy) + őľ n, where n = (dy, -dx). And we derived őľ = [ t_mid dy + (t_E t_F L + 4y0^2)/(4y0) ] / dx. This is messy but we can compute O explicitly.

Alternatively, we can use the formula for circumcenter in terms of coordinates: For points (x1,y1), (x2,y2), (x3,y3), the circumcenter is given by:

o_x = [ (x1^2+y1^2)(y2-y3) + (x2^2+y2^2)(y3-y1) + (x3^2+y3^2)(y1-y2) ] / [ 2(x1(y2-y3) + x2(y3-y1) + x3(y1-y2)) ]
o_y = [ (x1^2+y1^2)(x3-x2) + (x2^2+y2^2)(x1-x3) + (x3^2+y3^2)(x2-x1) ] / [ 2(x1(y2-y3) + x2(y3-y1) + x3(y1-y2)) ]

We can apply this to B=(x0,-y0), E=(x0+t_E dx, y0+t_E dy), F=(x0+t_F dx, y0+t_F dy). This might simplify because many terms have similar structure.

Let's denote:

For a point X = (x, y), define s(X) = x^2+y^2.

Then we need denominator D = 2( x_B(y_E-y_F) + x_E(y_F-y_B) + x_F(y_B-y_E) ) = 2( x_B(y_E-y_F) + x_E(y_F-y_B) + x_F(y_B-y_E) ).

Since y_E-y_F = t_E dy - t_F dy = (t_E - t_F) dy = - (t_F - t_E) dy = - (2d(p-x0)/L) dy? Actually, t_F - t_E = 2d(p-x0)/L. So y_E-y_F = - (2d(p-x0)/L) dy.

Also, y_F-y_B = (y0+t_F dy) - (-y0) = 2y0 + t_F dy.
y_B-y_E = (-y0) - (y0+t_E dy) = -2y0 - t_E dy.

Thus denominator:

D = 2[ x_B ( - (2d(p-x0)/L) dy ) + (x0+t_E dx) (2y0+t_F dy) + (x0+t_F dx) ( -2y0 - t_E dy) ].

Plug x_B = x0.

So D = 2[ - x0 * (2d(p-x0)/L) dy + (x0+t_E dx)(2y0+t_F dy) - (x0+t_F dx)(2y0+t_E dy) ].

Notice that (x0+t_E dx)(2y0+t_F dy) - (x0+t_F dx)(2y0+t_E dy) = Expand:

= x0(2y0+t_F dy) + t_E dx(2y0+t_F dy) - x0(2y0+t_E dy) - t_F dx(2y0+t_E dy) = x0(t_F dy - t_E dy) + t_E dx(2y0+t_F dy) - t_F dx(2y0+t_E dy) = x0 dy (t_F - t_E) + t_E dx 2y0 + t_E dx t_F dy - t_F dx 2y0 - t_F dx t_E dy = x0 dy (t_F - t_E) + 2y0 dx (t_E - t_F) + t_E t_F dx dy - t_E t_F dx dy = x0 dy (t_F - t_E) - 2y0 dx (t_F - t_E) = (t_F - t_E) ( x0 dy - 2y0 dx).

Thus D = 2[ - x0 * (2d(p-x0)/L) dy + (t_F - t_E) ( x0 dy - 2y0 dx) ].

But t_F - t_E = 2d(p-x0)/L. So:

D = 2[ - x0 * (2d(p-x0)/L) dy + (2d(p-x0)/L) ( x0 dy - 2y0 dx) ] = 2 * (2d(p-x0)/L) [ - x0 dy + x0 dy - 2y0 dx ] = 2 * (2d(p-x0)/L) [ -2y0 dx ] = -8y0 dx (p-x0)/L.

Thus D = -8y0 dx (p-x0)/L.

Now, note that p-x0 = dx. So D = -8y0 dx^2 / L.

Thus denominator D = -8y0 dx^2 / L.

Now, numerator for o_x: N_x = (x_B^2+y_B^2)(y_E-y_F) + (x_E^2+y_E^2)(y_F-y_B) + (x_F^2+y_F^2)(y_B-y_E).

Compute s_B = x0^2 + y0^2 = r^2.
s_E = (x0+t_E dx)^2 + (y0+t_E dy)^2 = x0^2 + 2x0 t_E dx + t_E^2 dx^2 + y0^2 + 2y0 t_E dy + t_E^2 dy^2 = r^2 + 2t_E (x0 dx + y0 dy) + t_E^2 L.
Similarly, s_F = r^2 + 2t_F (x0 dx + y0 dy) + t_F^2 L.

Now, y_E-y_F = (t_E - t_F) dy = - (t_F - t_E) dy = - (2d(p-x0)/L) dy = - (2d dx / L) dy (since p-x0=dx). So y_E-y_F = -2d dx dy / L.

y_F-y_B = (y0+t_F dy) - (-y0) = 2y0 + t_F dy.
y_B-y_E = (-y0) - (y0+t_E dy) = -2y0 - t_E dy.

Thus N_x = r^2 * (-2d dx dy / L) + s_E * (2y0+t_F dy) + s_F * (-2y0 - t_E dy).

= -2d r^2 dx dy / L + 2y0 (s_E - s_F) + dy (t_F s_E - t_E s_F).

= dy * (d x0 + d^2 - x0 - dx) + d y0 dy^2/dx + 2d r(p+r) dy/dx + d dy^2 t_E t_F/(4y0 dx).

o_y - h_y = d t_E t_F L/(4y0) + (d-p) y0/(x0+r).

Thus (o_y - h_y) dx = dx * [ d t_E t_F L/(4y0) + (d-p) y0/(x0+r) ].

Now, the cross product expression is:

(o_x - x0 - dx) dy - (o_y - h_y) dx = dy * (d x0 + d^2 - x0 - dx) + d y0 dy^2/dx + 2d r(p+r) dy/dx + d dy^2 t_E t_F/(4y0 dx) - dx * [ d t_E t_F L/(4y0) + (d-p) y0/(x0+r) ].

This is a mess. However, note that we also have the expression for the radius squared: (o_x - x0)^2 + (o_y + y0)^2. And we need to show that the square of the above equals L times that.

There is a known property: For two intersecting circles, the circle through B and the second intersections of a line through A with the circles is orthogonal to the circle with diameter AB. Let's test that: Circle with diameter AB: center (x0,0), radius y0. We already saw that it's not orthogonal to (BEF) in numeric. But maybe it's orthogonal to the circle through B, E, F? In numeric, O_BEF = (1,-1.2909), radius 0.816. Circle with diameter AB: center (0.25,0), radius 0.9682.
